News

National Army Recovers Xinji 61

The Right-Wing Army Encircles and Attacks the Jinjiazhai Bandit Nest, Which Can Be Taken Down Sooner or Later

Chiang Authorizes Xu Yuanquan to Handle Post-War Affairs in Central Hubei with Full Authority

Hankou Correspondence: Xinji is located on the border between Henan and Hubei, forming a three-legged strategic position with Huang'an Qiliping and Jinjiazhai in western Anhui, becoming an important nest for the Red bandits. This time, the central route army of the National Army launched an attack from both Henan and Hubei, adopting a large encirclement strategy, attacking from the north and south. First, they destroyed the key passes along the way, and then concentrated their forces to attack Xinji. At that time, the suppression of bandits in Anhui was successful, and the bandit troops were unable to take care of themselves, so reinforcements were cut off. However, the bandits relied on solid fortifications as a last resort, and knowing that their survival was at stake, they still tried their best to hold out against the National Army as a desperate measure. On the National Army's side, in addition to the troops of Liu Zhi, Zhang Fang, etc., advancing step by step from north to south and strictly preventing them from fleeing north, the troops of Wei Lihuang, advancing from the north and south, launched a fierce attack, facing the bandits head-on. From the 7th, they fought the bandits in a bloody battle for two days and nights. On the 9th, the bandit forces were unable to hold on and retreated completely. At 8 a.m. on that day, the Xinji bandit nest was completely recovered by Wei's army. All the pseudo-headquarters, arsenals, and military hospitals were destroyed. A large number of bandits were captured and killed, and a large number of guns were seized. Two "Marx" and "Lenin" aircraft were also captured. The remnants of the bandits fled eastward in a state of extreme distress. The aircraft reconnaissance report and Wei Junzhang's victory telegram have arrived in Wuhan today (10th). What they described is the same. With the Red bandits losing their stronghold, they can be wiped out in a matter of days. At the same time, the 5th Column of the Central Route Army began to attack Yingshan. On the 9th and 10th, they completely occupied the key passes near Yingshan County, one after another. The area is already under multiple encirclements and can be taken down soon. The 1st and 2nd Columns of the Right Route Army, taking advantage of the victory, pursued from Mabou. According to a telegram on the 10th, they have been pressing close to the Jinjiazhai bandit nest. All the fortifications built by the Red bandits have been destroyed by air force bombs and army artillery fire. Even if the bandits want to hold on to their defenses, they will not be able to. The recovery of Jinjiazhai is also just around the corner. According to the above, these places are all occupied by the Kwong Jixun's troops of the 4th Front Army of the Red bandits. The losses in the battles of Huoqiu, Huang'an, and Qiliping were enormous. Therefore, the National Army is like pulling up rotten wood and destroying dry weeds wherever it goes. The speed of progress is unprecedented. If Yingshan and Jinjiazhai are captured again, the Red bandits in that area will have no place to stand, and the devastated society of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui can gradually be restored. As for the Left Route Army, its only target is the He Long bandit gang, which has recently been driven into Honghu and heavily blockaded. Within the entire lake, only two mounds are still in the hands of the bandits. The rest have been occupied by Xu Yuanquan, Zhang Zhenhan, and other troops. Both the north and south banks of the Xiang River have long been cleared. Commander-in-Chief Chiang, considering that the bandit areas in that route have been largely recovered, and in order to facilitate the handling of post-war affairs, specially ordered Xu Yuanquan to handle everything with full authority. All local party and government officials and personnel responsible for clearing the countryside in the central Hubei area are under his immediate command, guidance, and supervision, so as to achieve the effect of using one's arms and fingers. (September 10th)

Legislative Yuan Revises the Law on Handling Labor-Management Disputes 62

(Continued)

Chapter 3: Procedures for Handling Labor-Management Disputes Section 1: Mediation Procedures (Article 21) When a party to a dispute applies for mediation, they shall submit a written application for mediation to the competent administrative agency. (Article 22) The application for mediation shall state the following matters: 1. The name, occupation, and address of the party, or the name and factory number of the business. If it is a group, its name and the location of its office; 2. The number of workers related to the dispute; 3. The key points of the dispute. (Article 23) When the competent administrative agency refers a matter for mediation without the application of a party to the dispute, the administrative agency shall notify both parties in writing of the matters to be mediated. (Article 24) The Mediation Committee shall begin investigating the following matters within two days of its convening: 1. The content of the dispute; 2. The written statements submitted by the parties to the dispute and other related matters; 3. The current situation of both parties to the dispute; 4. Other matters to be investigated. The investigation period shall not exceed seven days unless there are special circumstances. (Article 25) The Mediation Committee may, for the purpose of investigation, summon witnesses or order interested parties to attend the meeting to explain or submit written explanations. (Article 26) The Mediation Committee may investigate or inquire at related factories, shops, etc. (Article 27) Members of the Mediation Committee shall not disclose confidential matters obtained during the investigation. (Article 28) After the Mediation Committee completes the investigation, it shall make a decision on the mediation within two days, unless there are special circumstances or both parties to the dispute agree to postpone it. (Article 29) If the mediation of the Mediation Committee is agreed to by the representatives of both parties to the dispute and signed in the mediation record, the mediation shall be deemed established. The Mediation Committee shall report the results of the mediation to the competent administrative agency. Section 2: Arbitration Procedures (Article 30) When a party to a dispute applies for arbitration, they shall submit a written application for arbitration to the competent administrative agency. After receiving the application, the competent administrative agency shall promptly convene an Arbitration Committee at the location of the administrative agency or at the location of the dispute. (Article 31) When a party to a dispute applies for arbitration due to unsuccessful mediation, the application shall state the following matters: 1. The name, occupation, and address of the party, or the name and factory number of the business. If it is a group, its name and the location of its office; 2. The reasons for the unsuccessful mediation; 3. The purpose of the request. (Article 32) When both parties to a dispute apply for direct arbitration, their application shall state the matters listed in Article 24, item 1. (Article 33) The provisions of Articles 23 to 28 shall apply mutatis mutandis to the arbitration procedures. (Article 34) The arbitration of the Arbitration Committee shall be conducted by a consensus of all members and decided by a majority vote. The Arbitration Committee shall prepare a written arbitration award within two days of the arbitration and deliver it to both parties and submit it to the competent administrative agency for record. (Article 35) The parties to a dispute may reach a settlement regardless of the stage of the arbitration proceedings, but the terms of the settlement must be reported to the Arbitration Committee.

Chapter 4: Restrictions on the Conduct of Parties to a Dispute (Article 36) Employers or workers in the industries listed in Article 4 shall not suspend operations or strike due to any labor-management dispute. Employers or workers in other industrial and commercial enterprises shall not suspend operations or strike during the mediation period or when arbitration has been initiated. Employers shall not dismiss workers during the mediation or arbitration period. The start date of the mediation or arbitration period shall be calculated from the date the competent administrative agency notifies the parties to the dispute. (Article 37) Workers or workers' organizations shall not engage in the following acts: 1. Closing shops or factories; 2. Seizing or damaging goods or equipment of shops or factories without authorization; 3. Forcing others to strike.

Chapter 5: Penalties (Article 38) A party to a dispute who fails to comply with the decision or ruling deemed to be a contract between the parties to the dispute as stipulated in Article 3, Paragraph 2, and Article 7, Paragraph 2, shall be subject to a fine of two hundred yuan

Page 10

or detention of not more than forty days. In the preceding circumstances, the party to the dispute may separately request the court to enforce the decision directly in accordance with civil laws and regulations. (Article 39) When a party to a dispute violates the provisions of Articles 36 and 37, the competent administrative agency and the Mediation Committee or Arbitration Committee may stop them at any time. Those who disobey the stop may be fined not more than two hundred yuan. If the act constitutes a criminal offense, it shall still be punished in accordance with criminal law. (Article 40) Anyone who commits one of the following acts shall be subject to a fine of not more than one hundred yuan: 1. Violating the provisions of Article 25, failing to attend the meeting without justifiable reason, or failing to submit a written explanation; 2. Violating the provisions of Article 27. In the case of the second item above, if the act constitutes a criminal offense under criminal law, it shall still be punished in accordance with criminal law. (Article 41) Anyone who commits one of the following acts shall be subject to a fine of not more than one hundred yuan, but if the witness makes a false statement, they shall be punished in accordance with the provisions of criminal law regarding perjury: 1. Making a false statement in the circumstances stipulated in Article 25; 2. Refusing to investigate and answer or making a false statement without justifiable reason in the circumstances stipulated in Article 26. (Article 42) In the event of an act punishable under the provisions of each article of this chapter, the competent administrative agency and the Mediation Committee or Arbitration Committee may state the reasons and transfer the case to the competent court for review. The competent court shall, except in special circumstances, pronounce judgment within twenty days of receiving the case file.

Chapter 6: Supplementary Provisions (Article 43) The provincial government or the municipal government not under the jurisdiction of a province may, if necessary, formulate detailed rules for the implementation of this law and submit them to the National Government for approval. (Article 44) This law shall take effect from the date of its promulgation. Disputes that occurred before the promulgation of the amendments to this law but have not been resolved may be handled in accordance with this law.

Attached: Article 23 of the Revised Trade Union Law (Article 23) Disputes between labor and management shall not be declared as a strike unless they have gone through mediation procedures and are approved by a two-thirds majority of all members in a secret ballot at the members' meeting. If arbitration has been initiated or is required by law, a strike shall still not be declared. Trade unions shall not endanger public order and safety or endanger the life and property of employers or others during strikes. Trade unions shall not demand wage increases exceeding the standard wage and declare a strike. Trade unions organized by workers in the industries listed in Article 3 shall not declare a strike.

Bandit Atmosphere in Lu and Tong Counties of Anhui Province Gradually Subsides 63

Tang Yunshan's Brigade Ordered to Advance and Suppress

Yingshan County Placed Under Hubei Jurisdiction

Anqing Correspondence: The bandits in Anhui Province, Zhang Da Bizi and Quan Guangyi's troops, were previously recruited by a certain army. Later, due to lack of supplies, they relapsed into their old ways and looted Jinniu Town in Lujiang County and Kongcheng Town in Tongcheng County, one after another. Recently, Chiang Kai-shek, Commander-in-Chief of the Bandit Suppression in Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, specially telegraphed the Independent 33rd Brigade of Tang Yunshan to temporarily be under the command of the provincial government and ordered Tang's brigade to send troops to suppress the bandits in the Shuhe area. Tang's brigade had just arrived in Anhui from western Anhui after suppressing bandits, so they immediately dispatched two battalions of Ni Rongxian's regiment and the entire Liu's regiment to block and suppress them. The defense of the provincial capital was also taken over by Tang's troops because the 5th Regiment of the Military Police of Zhang Benqing was ordered to go to Nanjing. Later, Tang's brigade received an order from the Military Commission that the training team of the Central Military Academy was about to concentrate on training in Wuhu. The remaining defense of Datong was originally intended to be taken over by Tang's brigade. Now Tang's brigade must take over the defense after the bandit suppression is completed. As for the bandits in Tongcheng, after being pursued and suppressed by Ni's regiment, progress has been quite rapid. However, Yu Yuying, the magistrate of Tongcheng County, was kidnapped while leading troops in hot pursuit. The bandits demanded recruitment as a condition for his release. The provincial government has now temporarily appointed Wang Weixia as a substitute to avoid a situation where no one is in charge. As for Lujiang, the city defense suddenly became strained a few days ago due to the bandits' attempt to attack the city. Tang's brigade ordered the advancing troops to suppress the bandits according to the original plan and telegraphed the neighboring county teams to block and intercept them at key points. Brigade Commander Tang also went to Luting to supervise the battle, hoping to annihilate them as soon as possible. The provincial government received a telegram from the General Headquarters for Bandit Suppression in Henan, Hubei, and Anhui stating that Yingshan County, which belongs to Anhui Province, is adjacent to Luotian Chishui in Hubei Province. The county seat is located upstream of Chishui, which is beyond the reach of the administrative power of Anhui Province. For the convenience of clearing and suppressing bandits and handling post-war affairs, it is temporarily placed under the jurisdiction of the Third Administrative Inspectorate of Hubei Province. This has been submitted to the provincial government's regular meeting on the 9th for compliance. (September 11th)

Jiangsu Province Sets a Deadline for Supplementary Land Prices 64

A three-month deadline from the date of the announcement

Failure to pay by the deadline will result in the confiscation of half of the land

Regarding the case of supplementary land prices for developed land in Jiangsu Province, the Department of Finance previously ordered the financial bureaus of various counties to consult with the county government, consider local conditions, and collect a large sum of money within three months to alleviate urgent needs. However, the reports and remittances from various bureaus have been scarce, and the deadline has now passed. The Department of Finance believes that the need for funds is urgent and cannot be delayed any further. Yesterday, it ordered various counties to continue to follow the previously agreed-upon method of urging payment and to announce it in conjunction with the Sand Land Bureau. The original resolution on urging payment of supplementary land prices for developed land is recorded as follows: "For old cases before May 18th of the Republic of China where land prices have not been paid, in accordance with the order of the ministry, land prices shall be collected regardless of whether the land has been enclosed and developed. Various bureaus shall issue a public notice in conjunction with the county government's land bureau, setting a strict deadline (from the date of the announcement to three months) for implementation. If households fail to pay by the deadline, the assumed disposal methods are as follows: 1. The county government's land bureau shall order the households that have failed to pay the land price to be arrested and detained as a warning; 2. The county government's land bureau shall take away the households' business licenses and issue tax certificates for half of the land. The remaining half shall be taken back by the bureau and put up for sale; 3. The county government's land bureau shall seal off and harvest the half of the land to be taken back. Violators will be severely punished; 4. The half of the land to be disposed of shall be put up for sale by the bureau. If someone claims it, the original claiming household shall be strictly prevented from obstructing. Violators will be severely punished. The original claiming household shall not demand compensation for expenses such as enclosure fees for the land from the claiming household in order to avoid disputes. The above methods shall be implemented separately by various bureaus after considering local conditions."

Record of a Journey to the West (II) (X)

Inspection of Oil and Coal Mines 65

At 9:00 AM on the 28th, the team leader Hu Chuanyuan and team members Ma Jinhong, Jing Lan, Hu Jue-wen, Gu Zhizhong, Zhu Rui-jie, Zhu Qiqing, Shen Yiqian, and others, a total of ten people, rode horses, mules, and donkeys, crossed the gurgling Luo River, and arrived at Qiao'ergou to inspect the oil mine, and at Liuwanjiagou to inspect the coal mine. Qiao'ergou is located seven li east of the county seat. We rode our horses quickly and arrived at the town in less than an hour. The so-called oil mine is located near the Catholic Church established by Spanish missionaries in the area. The mine was jointly exploited by China and the United States in February of the third year of the Republic of China. The well is about thirty zhang deep and produces about thirty catties of oil per day. Because the quantity was too small, further work was ordered to dig deeper in the hope of obtaining a large amount of oil. Unexpectedly, the result of digging deeper was only sand. The mine was unable to sustain itself and was shut down in September of that year. What we saw at that time was that the wellhead of the mine was completely covered by yellow soil, and the ground was covered with vegetables, with no trace of an oil mine. According to the locals, there was nothing to be seen when it rained, but oil appeared in times of drought, which shows that there is still a considerable amount of oil underground.

At 11:00 AM, Hu Boyuan, Ma Jinhong, Jing Lan, Zhu Ruijie, and I, a total of five people, continued to proceed to Liuwanjiagou. The remaining people returned to their residences in the city. Ten minutes later, it rained heavily. We rested in a small village and had some food. At 12:00, it seemed that the sky had cleared after the rain, so we continued to proceed to our destination. After a hundred or so steps, dark clouds suddenly gathered and the rain started again. We did not care and proceeded even faster. We arrived at Liuwanjiagou in a short time. The ditch is about fifteen li from the city. There are currently two operating coal mines, one of which has been abandoned and cannot be used. The other was working when we arrived. The well is in a mud-roofed stone-walled house, about twenty-three zhang deep. There were six workers next to the well winding coal upwards. There were thirteen workers underground using tools to mine coal. The tunnel is only about three chi high, so the miners underground cannot lie down inside. They must enter early and leave late, unlike other places where they can work underground for more than ten days without coming out. The coal seam is about two chi thick and is two layers connected, with no stones or sand in between. The quality of the coal is average. According to experts, the coal contains a lot of ash and is mixed with pyrite, the amount of which is about 20%. The workers work in shifts of about six or seven people. Each shift is required to produce about 134 baskets of coal, each basket weighing about forty catties. All of them are sold locally and not elsewhere. The average daily wage for workers is about 60 cents, while those who wind coal are paid about 30 cents per day, and those who go down the well are paid about 90 cents. The price of coal is about 40 cents per hundred catties. There is accumulated water in the well. About forty bags of water can be pumped out every night using a cowhide bag. There are two roads in the well, one flat and one slightly inclined, running southwest for about ten zhang. The wellhead is round, with a major diameter of six chi and a minor diameter of four chi, and cost about 1,000 yuan to dig. Charcoal is burned next to the well to send hot air to the well below for ventilation. The coal is wound from the bottom of the well to the ground, which takes about two minutes each time.

In addition to Qiao'ergou, oil seepage has also been found in Xijiazhuang, Dengjiagou in the western district of the county, and Long'ersi in the southern district. In addition to the aforementioned Liujiagou coal mine, there are also coal mines in Cuijiage, forty-five li northeast of the county, Baijiaya Village, thirty-five li northeast of the county, and Panlong Village, twenty-five li southeast of the county. They have already been exploited. The coal is black and smoky. The coal area is about twenty square li, with reserves of about fourteen trillion tons.

After the investigation was completed at 2:00 PM, it rained heavily again. The mud roads were slippery and impassable. Mr. Hong Jinglan fell and got up again and again. The situation only improved slightly after leaving the ditch, but when the horses galloped, the mud and water splashed on our clothes, which made us feel quite embarrassed.

Small Factories and Others 66

In addition to mineral products, Fushi has four small factories, which were surveyed as follows: 1. Fuxingde Felt Workshop: The felt produced is three chi wide and five chi long. Each felt requires three catties of wool and one catty of millet flour. Five pieces of felt can be made per day. The workshop has five workers. The wages are about six or seven yuan per month. Each person makes about one piece of felt per day. 2. Yongji Carpet Factory: The carpet produced is two chi wide and four chi long, with 100 stitches. One carpet requires one catty of raw materials (including miscellaneous materials), five catties of light wool, and one catty of thread. There are four looms. Each carpet requires ten man-days to make and about three yuan in wages. 3. Yufeng Sock Factory: There are four machines. Thirty pairs of socks can be produced per day. The sock thread is of two types, 42-count and 16-count, both from Shanxi. The price is 12-13 yuan per package for 42-count and 7 yuan per package for 16-count. Each package can make 4-5 dozen socks, and each dozen sells for 3.5 yuan. 4. Yishun Carpet Factory: The carpet woven is three chi wide and five chi long, with 100 stitches. Each piece costs 24 yuan. Generally, each square chi requires one catty of wool at a cost of 20 cents per catty. Each worker only weaves three or four inches per day. It takes twenty man-days to make one carpet, and the cost is about 20 yuan. The cost of dyes is about 50 cents per catty, and the dyeing fee for each 14 catties of wool (i.e., one carpet) is about 2 yuan. The factory has four workers and two looms. Each worker can weave one catty of thread per day.

Other information is as follows: 1. The total area of the county is 5,600 square li, and the total population is over 21,000 people. 2. There is a natural forest in the Nangou area of the southern district, covering an area of about 12 square li. 3. The mountains produce many medicinal herbs, such as Artemisia capillaris, Leonurus japonicus, Xanthium sibiricum, Anemarrhena asphodeloides, Prunus armeniaca, Lycium chinense, Tussilago farfara, Taraxacum mongolicum, Pharbitis nil, Foeniculum vulgare, Dolichos lablab, Oxalis corniculata, Ephedra sinica, Dioscorea opposita, Sophora japonica, Spiraea japonica, Euphorbia humifusa, and Cicada slough. 4. The furs include cattle, sheep, foxes, and wolves. The local livestock breeding industry is quite prosperous, and a large amount of white and black wool is produced. Special products include Russula vinosa and others. 5. In terms of historical sites, the Huayuantou area in the southern district is full of peonies, which were planted by Du Fu of the Tang Dynasty when he took refuge from the war and lived in seclusion. Ten li north of the county seat is where Di Qing of the Song Dynasty was imprisoned. The place is still called Di Qing Prison, and the remains are still there. In addition, Fan Zhongyan's large-character calligraphy in Jialing and Fan Gong's Well in Nanzhai are also very famous.

Huang Bokui Returns 67

Mr. Huang Bokui separated from us in Yijun to investigate the coal mines in the countryside alone with a donkey. It has been seven days since he left, and he has not yet returned to the team. Some team members were worried about accidents. On the afternoon of the 28th, Mr. Huang suddenly rushed back. Everyone was overjoyed to see him again. Mr. Huang's trip was very successful. His report is disclosed below.

I (Huang said, the same below) heard the Director of the Bureau of Construction in Yijun say that the coal mine in Yishicun, 110 li west of the county, has a coal seam that is more than three zhang thick, the coal mine in Jiaoping Town, 50 li west of the county, has a coal seam that is about seven or eight chi thick, and the coal mine in Qilitun, 90 li north of the county, has a coal seam that is about four chi thick. Therefore, on the 22nd, I separated from the team in Yijun and went to investigate. County Magistrate Zhang Doushan sent a police officer and two soldiers to protect me. I departed from Yijun at 9:00 AM and rested once after traveling 22 li west. At the 25-li point, I reached a temple. The police officer asked to rest again, and I reluctantly agreed. Unexpectedly, the police officer slept soundly in the temple for two hours. After I repeatedly urged him, he slowly proceeded. I arrived at Jiping Town at 4:00 PM. The distance from Yijun to here is 50 li. There is a battalion of defense troops stationed there. There are no more troops stationed further west. The Yijun County District Office is located here. The district chief, Yan, is illiterate. It is said that Koukou is located another five or sixty li away and appears and disappears unpredictably. Jiaozhen has been occupied three times. It is now reported that Koukou has been found in Phoenix Mountain, about 30 li from the town. I shouldn't be able to go to Yishicun, I should sleep with my clothes on tonight, and escape east as soon as I hear gunfire. The situation seems very tense. I entrusted him to introduce a miner who had worked in Yishicun to talk. The miner came to see me in the evening. I asked him about the coal mine in Yishicun, which uses a straight well to wind coal. The well is 12-13 zhang to 15-16 zhang deep. The thickness of the coal seam varies greatly. The thickest is three zhang, and the thinnest is over one zhang. There is gas in the mine that can ignite spontaneously, so more than one well has been abandoned because of this. Some also stopped due to water. The coal is sold on the mine at a price of three corners of the ocean per load (200-300 catties) and is sold in the areas of Xi'an, Sanyuan, Fuping, and Yaoxian. I asked if there were any coal mines nearby. It is said that the Cuijiagou, 20 li west of the town, is currently producing coal. The next morning (23rd), I discussed with District Chief Yan to ask him to send someone to guide me. Yan strongly advised me not to go, saying that Cuijiagou is located at the foot of Phoenix Mountain, and he could not be responsible. Moreover, the situation of the mine has already been explained in detail by the miners, and there is absolutely no difference in what I would see and hear if I went to investigate, so it is not worth going. I told him that I came specifically to investigate coal mines, and it would be a pity if I couldn't see them with my own eyes. Therefore, I decided to go. Yan then sent three militiamen to protect me, and the three soldiers sent by the county government also went with me. After traveling 10 li west to Yaoxian Village, I saw a coal kiln about one li west of the village. The situation is as follows:

1. A straight well is four chi in diameter and twenty-five chi deep. There is accumulated water in the well. Water is currently being drawn out with wooden buckets, one bucket at a time, about 30 catties per bucket. Coal cannot be produced. The well is dug down through mud. There is no rock above the coal seam. Four or five workers are used to dig every day. It took three months to see coal. The wages are three corners of the ocean. The cost is about 100 yuan in total. There are no supports.

2. A sloping well is dug towards the northeast, with a slope of about 30 degrees and a slope length of 35-36 chi. There is no water. There is currently one miner digging, and the coal he digs is split equally between him and the owner.

Director Dong Xiujia of the Jiangsu Construction Department Discusses Construction Projects 68

Detailed Explanation of Submitting Half of the Land Tax for Road Construction to the Province

Plans to Build Ten Main Roads, Requiring an Estimated Budget of Over Seven Million

Subsidies for Various Counties to Dredge Rivers and Repair Embankments, Approximately 700,000 Yuan

Yesterday, while traveling to Shanghai on business, this reporter happened to share a car with Dong Xiujia, the Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department. I took the opportunity to engage in a thorough conversation and inquire about the recent issue of Jiangsu Province's counties submitting half of the land tax for road construction to the province. Director Dong provided detailed answers, which are recorded below.

I asked: "It is said that some counties have raised objections to the decision that all counties in Jiangsu Province should submit half of the land tax for road construction to the province, to be used as funding for national and provincial road construction. Is this true?"

Director Dong replied: "Recently, counties such as Wuxi, Taicang, and Baoshan have stated that submitting half of the land tax for road construction to the province is inconsistent with the original plan and suspect that provincial funds are being used for county purposes. They have sent telegrams to the province to stop this. However, this is largely due to misunderstandings. The provincial government has already issued explanations, and many enlightened individuals in the counties, after careful consideration, can readily resolve these issues."

I asked: "Is the land tax for road construction specifically intended for the construction of county roads? Now, half of it is being submitted to the province for the construction of national and provincial roads. Is this inconsistent with the original plan's nature?"

Director Dong replied: "The decision to collect land tax for road construction was made in the winter of the 17th year of the Republic (1928-1929). However, at that time, the highway plan was not yet complete, so there was no distinction between national and provincial roads. Later, due to the varying lengths of roads, the shortest roads were designated as county roads, those passing through two or more counties were designated as provincial roads, and those passing through two or more provinces were designated as national roads. In fact, both provincial and national roads pass through the boundaries of various counties and serve as county roads. The reason why it was not named 'county road land tax' but 'land tax for road construction' is precisely because of this. Moreover, in terms of the definitions of national, provincial, and county roads, they are merely indicative of main and branch lines and do not have special distinctions. Since all national and provincial road lines inevitably traverse the jurisdictions of various counties, dividing them into segments essentially makes them the main trunk lines of county roads. Without trunk lines, what benefit do branch lines have? The relationship with trunk lines is more important than any other branch lines. Therefore, using half of the land tax to fund construction is no different from each county constructing its county roads. Furthermore, recently, when constructing roads such as the Chu-Su Provincial Road and the Hu-Hang Provincial Road, counties through which the routes passed all allocated land tax to fund the projects. All counties were happy to contribute, and the records are available. No one has raised objections. This further demonstrates that the province-wide land tax for road construction is intended for the construction of roads throughout the province and is not divided based on the names of national, provincial, and county roads to be mutually exclusive. Moreover, the original plan for collecting land tax for road construction in the winter of the 17th year of the Republic was approved by the 103rd meeting of the provincial government. It stipulated that the collected funds 'should be remitted to the Construction Department monthly for special storage and not be diverted for other uses.' The intention was that highways are an integrated whole, and it is necessary to concentrate financial resources for the overall development. If the province does not have the authority to统筹 (tǒng chóu, overall planning and coordination) and allocate, why would there be such an unnecessary regulation at that time? Later, to facilitate the management of funds, the Construction Administration Conference decided that each county should manage the funds themselves, and the method of remitting funds to the province was temporarily not implemented. Now, remitting half of the land tax to the province for management and use is to promote the development of highways in the province in a way that meets the needs and is in line with the original plan for collecting land tax, without any conflict. Moreover, Zhejiang Province has precedents for collecting an additional 10% on land tax compensation from each county for highways, as well as special construction taxes, which are all remitted to the province for management and use. This is not unique to Jiangsu. Therefore, those who believe that the plan to submit half of the land tax to the province is a change to the original plan are unaware that this method was stipulated several years ago and is only being implemented now."

I asked: "The land tax for road construction has not been remitted to the province according to the original plan for several years. Why is it now being remitted by half?"

Director Dong replied: "In the past, road construction in each county was managed independently, with little coordination. Road construction mainly focused on development within their own boundaries, with fragmented and piecemeal efforts. They rarely focused on the main trunk lines connecting the counties, leading to a situation where there were only branch lines without trunk lines. Highway transportation values connection and accessibility. Now, with only branch lines and no trunk lines, the priorities have been misplaced. Therefore, over the past four or five years, millions have been spent, but the highways in various counties of the province have shown little progress. Traffic obstruction remains the same, which is due to this. It is extremely regrettable. The Shanghai Incident this spring led to frequent military transport to the rear, and military roads were built day and night, fearing it would be too late. This shows the failure of previous work. If we do not seek other ways to improve and continue with the old rules, no matter how much money each county spends, there will be no progress in transportation. The Construction Department is responsible for the construction administration of the entire province, so we have specifically sought improvement. From now on, the construction of highways in the province must be planned comprehensively, and the urgency of each project must be determined based on the needs. We must ensure that the main trunk lines are completed first to avoid the previous fragmented and obstructive practices."

I asked: "After the previous explanation, it is clear that the nature of the land tax for road construction has not changed. Why do counties like Wuxi still consider the portion remitted to the province as changing county funds to provincial funds?"

Director Dong replied: "The land tax for road construction was originally designated for road construction. Although half of it is now remitted to the province, it is not being used for administrative expenses, nor is it considered provincial funds. It is still a special fund stored specifically for road construction and cannot be diverted for other uses. Even if it were not remitted to the province, each county would still be responsible for building national and provincial roads. Now, it is simply changing the county's custody procedures to the province's custody procedures. It has not been changed to provincial funds. The original plan for remittance to the province stipulates this in detail. It seems very appropriate to use the funds for road construction in this province for road projects in this province. It would be a misunderstanding to refer to it as changing county funds to provincial funds."

I asked: "How will this remitted half of the land tax be used in the future?"

Director Dong replied: "Road construction projects require a lot of funding, and the financial resources of each county vary. In the past, each county was managed independently. County A, if it had funds, would build roads in County A. County B, if it had funds, would build roads in County B. There was little coordination. If two wealthy counties were separated by a poor county, the traffic between the three counties would never be connected. This is the most serious consequence of this approach. From now on, we will plan comprehensively and handle matters based on the needs. This year, we will use the collected funds to build trunk roads in counties A and B. Next year, we can use the collected funds to build trunk roads in counties C and D. Although there will be a sequence of implementation, there will be no preferential treatment in the allocation of funds. We expect that within three years, highway transportation throughout the province will be unhindered, and the public will not be disappointed."

I asked: "Which are the main roads to be built this year, and what is the estimated cost?"

Director Dong replied: "There are currently ten main roads to be built, requiring an estimated budget of over seven million yuan." (At this point, Director Dong showed a list of planned highways and costs.) "Relying solely on land tax is insufficient. The National Economic Commission has also agreed to lend funds from the provincial road construction fund, which is a considerable amount. However, the condition is that the province must be able to raise sufficient funds to start construction before the loan is granted. This is a rare opportunity that will greatly benefit the development of highways in the province. If we miss this opportunity, it will be difficult to raise large amounts of funds elsewhere. Therefore, the method of submitting half of the land tax for road construction to the province is the only way to develop public road projects in the province."

I asked: "What is the situation with the counties reporting and submitting half of the land tax for road construction recently?"

Director Dong replied: "Since the announcement of this plan, more than forty counties throughout the province have reported that they will comply. More than ten counties have submitted daily and monthly reports of collections. Some counties have already remitted the July collections. In general, all counties understand the overall situation, and we can be optimistic about future remittances. Although a few local groups in the counties have some misunderstandings and doubts, the provincial government has repeatedly explained the matter carefully, and we believe they will fully understand."

Attached is a list of planned highway construction expenditures for Jiangsu Province this year:

Item Estimated Expenditure

Su-Jia Road (Wujiang Section) 868,106 Yuan

Su-Jia Road (Wuxian Section) 150,000 Yuan

Jing-Hu Road (Xi-Hu Section) 1,317,000 Yuan

Jing-Si Road 590,000 Yuan

Dong-Chu Road 1,284,700 Yuan

Jiang-Huai Road 927,500 Yuan

Jiang-Ju Road 308,517 Yuan

Huai-Pi Road 949,000 Yuan

Huai-Hai Road 878,000 Yuan

Jiangyin-Changshu Road 715,800 Yuan

Total 7,986,677 Yuan

I asked: "Jiangsu Province is an agricultural region. Construction projects should focus on water conservancy. Why is your department planning to construct so many highways this year? Many people have doubts. Can you explain the rationale?"

Director Dong replied: "Agriculture and water conservancy are closely related. Therefore, this department pays special attention to water conservancy projects in various counties. Last year, when various counties in Jiangnan and Jiangbei organized work relief projects, this department approved and allocated special construction funds such as land tax for road construction to subsidize the counties in dredging rivers. We are currently formulating detailed plans, regulations, and fundraising strategies. We plan to order all county magistrates and directors of construction bureaus to fully mobilize and start work after October. If the waterways cannot be completed this year, dredging will continue next winter to ensure that the province's rivers are clear, providing the benefits of irrigation in drought years and preventing flooding in wet years. Although road construction may seem unrelated to agriculture on the surface, it is actually a way to develop agriculture. The value of agricultural products lies in their ability to be sold in various markets. If transportation is inconvenient, even if water conservancy is well-maintained and agricultural products are abundant, if they cannot be transported to various places for sale, the income of farmers will not increase. Furthermore, banditry has been rampant in various places recently. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Military Affairs Commission believes that to eliminate bandits, roads must first be built to facilitate military operations. Therefore, most of the above roads were ordered to be built urgently by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and the Ministry of Military Affairs. After examining the actual situation, areas with difficult transportation are often areas where bandits are rampant. Therefore, for the sake of the province's security, it is necessary to actively build roads."

Local Correspondence

Taicang 69

Xijitai Pawnshop Announces Liquidation

The Xijitai Pawnshop in the city has had poor business in recent years, with losses reaching over 300,000 yuan. After the January 28th Shanghai Incident, all money houses stopped dealing with each other, and the money market was extremely tight. The pawnshop stopped lending and redeeming due to financial difficulties. Recently, as the owner has no intention of continuing the business, liquidation was announced on September 8th. The remaining goods are valued at 17,000 yuan. From the 25th, a three-month grace period will be given for redemption at a discount, after which the goods will be appraised and sold.

Suzhou 70

Notorious Bandit Wu Xiaopangzi Sentenced to Death

The notorious Anhui gang bandit Wu Xiaopangzi, also known as Hu Zhanghe, was formerly a small leader under Wu Dajinzi, the leader of the Anhui gang. In the winter of the 17th year of the Republic (1928-1929), he opened fire on the water police in Qingpu, killing Captain Zhang Sida. In the 19th year of the Republic (1930), he committed a series of kidnapping and robbery cases in Qingpu. The Qingpu County Government offered a reward of 300 yuan for his capture. He was captured by the First District Water Police on August 30th at the Longwang Temple in Zhujing and sent to the Bandit Suppression Headquarters, which sentenced him to death. The sentence has been submitted to the province for review.

Lawyer and Doctor File Reciprocal Lawsuits

Ma Chongyan, a lawyer residing at No. 31, Cunfang Lane, Shanghai, sued female obstetrician Shen Xiaoxue in the Wuxian District Court for negligence during his wife's childbirth. Shen also hired lawyer Wu Chao to sue Ma for obstructing her practice. The court held a hearing on the afternoon of September 9th. Finding the plaintiff's allegations without merit, the court advised both parties to attempt reconciliation.

Series of Robberies and Kidnappings in Xishan Township

More than ten bandits arrived at the home of Ma Renshan in Xishan Township, Dongting, at dawn on the 10th, indiscriminately looting and causing losses of about 500 to 600 yuan. The bandits then went to the home of Zhang Ashui in the neighboring village, looted his property, and kidnapped Zhang's son, Ah Er, towards Taihu Lake.

Wuxi 71

Arrest of Gang of Robbers of Sailing Vessels

County Magistrate Chen recently, due to the constant occurrence of robberies on land and water in both urban and rural areas, is deeply concerned about the future of public security. He has strictly ordered his subordinates to cooperate in arresting the criminals within a limited time. Xue Furui, the captain of the Detective Squad of the County Public Security Bureau, upon receiving the order, immediately led Detectives Dai and Shen, as well as all the detectives, to investigate separately. On the 7th of this month, Captain Xue received a tip from an informant and immediately set out, first arresting Liu Desheng near the Yuchang Silk Factory outside the South Gate, and then Zhou Yongchang, another robber, in front of the Qian Shen Silk Factory. Both were taken into custody for strict interrogation and confessed to the truth about the robbery. He immediately followed the locations provided and investigated separately. Until dawn yesterday morning, he intercepted a stolen boat under the Miaogang Bridge in the East Gate, arresting Li Fuwan, a robber who participated in the robbery of Shen Jianhua's sailing vessel from Suzhou to Yuqi Town in this county on the 4th of this month, as well as two female bandits, Li Xue and Zhu Ji. A pistol, two axes, a wallet, six pawn tickets, seventeen large and small straw mats, and gray cloth military uniforms, military hats, burlap sacks, etc., totaling dozens of items, were found on the boat. Yesterday, all were taken to the Detective Squad for safekeeping. Captain Xue thoroughly interrogated the suspects, who confessed to the robbery of the Yuqi sailing vessel. In the afternoon, the five male and female bandits were presented to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau Begins Tax Collection

The Ministry and Provincial authorities have been competing to manage the tobacco and alcohol license tax. Recently, the Executive Yuan ordered the Provincial Government to cancel the original proposal and return the collection to the Ministry of Finance. All tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus established by the provinces, branches in various districts, and collection offices in various counties were ordered by the Ministry of Finance to transfer the order to the Finance Department for immediate cancellation. It has been learned that Chen Henian, the selected commissioner of the Jiangsu Stamp, Tobacco, and Alcohol Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, has been appointed as the director of the Wuxi Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Branch Bureau. The bureau's address has been found at No. 1, Changle Lane, Wanqian Road, outside Guangfu Gate, and it was officially established yesterday (the 11th). He took office and announced to tobacco and alcohol merchants the commencement of the collection of the autumn tobacco and alcohol license tax. If tobacco and alcohol merchants have already paid taxes to the bureaus established by the former Finance Department and have obtained licenses, they are allowed to use the tax amount on the face of the licenses to offset the current payment and re-obtain the autumn licenses in accordance with the levels stipulated in the regulations promulgated by the Ministry. Such flexible tax payment methods ensure that tobacco and alcohol merchants do not suffer losses. Those who have not paid taxes should promptly pay taxes and obtain licenses in accordance with the regulations to facilitate business operations.

Changzhou 72

Two Businesses Bombed

At 6:50 PM on the 10th, while the shop assistants were organizing fabrics at the Tianfengtai Silk and Foreign Goods Store in Xiying Lane, Wuyi, a loud bang was suddenly heard, and the area was filled with smoke. A copper ring was found on the floor under the awning, with many broken steel pieces scattered around. Three of the glass panes on the counter were also broken. Deputy Manager Qiu Bingchen and student Cheng Haoyuan both suffered minor injuries to their left legs and were sent to Wujin Hospital for treatment before being discharged. Around 8:00 PM on the same night, two people entered the Zhenxin Cloth Factory in Sanjiangjun Lane, Dongxiatang, and threw three bombs. One landed on the door, and two landed on the wall, all of which were pierced through. On their way out, they threw two or three more bombs in the lane, but no one was injured. The bombings of the two businesses shocked the city. Afterwards, the newspaper received a notice from the Wujin Anti-Japanese and Eliminate Traitors Group, stating that the bombings were the group's action to punish traitorous merchants.

Murderer in Strangulation Case Apprehended

Yun Fukang, a cattle thief who escaped from the Third Branch Bureau of the Wuyi Xiahe Public Security Bureau, was strangled to death and his body was dumped in the river that night. The branch bureau apprehended the murderers, Du Yusan, Yun Liansheng, etc., and sent them to the court for interrogation. Yun Rongda, another suspect, was found to have fled to the home of Zhu Xizhen at No. 30, Changle Lane, Hengfeng Road, Zhabei, Shanghai. Patrolman Luo Guanghua was sent to Shanghai to cooperate with the local police in apprehending him. He was then sent to Changzhou and transferred to the County Court for investigation yesterday.

Yangzhou 73

Observations Amidst Rumors of Opium Monopoly

Although the opium monopoly in Jiangsu Province has been denied by the authorities, the relevant monopoly agencies in Jiangbei have been established one after another. This county, as the hub for sales in Jiangbei, has established an office in the Chen Residence on Gengzi Street in the city. The name of the agency is "Suzhou Yangzhou Branch of the Special Tax Office for Cleaning Up Certain Two Provinces." The person in charge is a Mr. Ling, named Director. There is also a Mr. Zhou in charge of foreign affairs, and a Mr. Jiang in charge of internal affairs. There are also several section chiefs, section members, clerks, chief inspectors, and inspectors, totaling more than twenty people. It is said that twelve official opium houses have been designated in Yangzhou City, each of which must first pay a license fee and business tax of 600 yuan, followed by a monthly business tax of 300 yuan. Regarding cargo transportation protection, a transportation fee of 2 jiao per tael and a stamp duty of 1 jiao must be paid. The office has also drafted a "Declaration Form" and distributed it to the original opium vendors in Yangzhou City to fill out.

Gaoyou 74

Zhang Burong Killed by Bandits

Zhang Burong, a resident of Zhuzhuang Township, Tenth District of the county, was chatting with his neighbors in the rice field a few days ago when two men in short shirts suddenly arrived. They took out pistols and said to Zhang, "Are you Zhang Burong? Our battalion commander is waiting for you." As they spoke, they dragged Zhang away. When they reached halfway, he refused to go any further. Another bandit then drew out a sharp blade and stabbed a hole in Zhang's nose, threaded it with a rope, and dragged him along. When they reached the southern wilderness, about two li from Zhang's house, another bandit came and said to Zhang, "You're here? We're inviting you back to your hometown today." After speaking, he raised his gun and fired four shots in a row, killing Zhang. After Zhang died, they used a large knife to cut off his limbs and head. It is said that Zhang's wife has reported to the county government requesting the arrest of the murderers.

Ningbo 75

Kidnapping Case Occurs in Yinzhou West

Zhu Arui, a wealthy resident of Huangzhaodi, near Huang Xinglin, Guilin Township, Yinzhou West, was suddenly attacked by more than ten bandits at about 9 PM last night. They broke into the house. Arui and his eldest son heard the alarm and fled, but his second son was unable to escape because his wife had just given birth. He was tied up by the bandits. His wife, seeing her husband being tied up, knelt on the ground and begged, angering the bandits. They brutally beat her with weapons. Fearing that she would be beaten to death, she jumped down from the building, causing serious injuries. The bandits then took her husband away, leaving a letter demanding a large ransom for his release.

Man Loses Gambling Debt, Steals, Falls from Building, and Dies

A woman surnamed Jiang from Jiangjiawantou, Yuyao, had two sons who were merchants in Shanghai. The other day, she stole three bolts of lake crepe silk from her cohabitant, Zhong, because she lost gambling. She planned to pawn the silk to pay off her gambling debts. Zhong, after being stolen, knew that no outsiders had entered and concluded that it was an inside job. He reported to the police station, who searched Jiang's house and found the stolen goods. Jiang, knowing that she had no face to show, jumped from the building to end her life, injuring her head severely. She died yesterday after ineffective treatment.

Xiaoshan 76

Sacrificing Two Lives Due to Gambling Debts

Lu Jifa, a sandman from Sanchalu, East Township, Xiaoshan, has been making a living from gambling. This autumn, he has repeatedly lost gambling, resulting in heavy debts. On the 9th, he committed suicide by hanging himself because he was unable to repay his gambling debts. His wife, returning from outside, saw him and tried to save him, but he had already died. The next morning, his wife tried to borrow silver dollars from her mother's family to buy a coffin for her husband, but she accidentally fell into the water and drowned while traveling to Nanyang by boat, resulting in the deaths of both husband and wife. This is truly a tragic story.

Autonomy Household Tax Causes Widespread Resentment

The implementation of the autonomy household tax in various districts, townships, and towns in Xiaoshan is plagued with corruption. Cunning township chiefs dare to collect taxes privately or issue private receipts. The district offices do not report their annual income to the county government. The people's hard-earned money is almost completely plundered, but there is no significant achievement in autonomy work. Therefore, the general public is full of resentment towards this household tax.

Outline for Improving Jiangsu Normal Education Plan 78

(1)

The Jiangsu Education Department has drafted an outline for improving normal education throughout Jiangsu Province. This outline has been approved by the Department's administrative meeting and submitted to the Provincial Government's Ministry of Education for record. The outline is recorded below:

Outline for Improving Normal Education Throughout Jiangsu Province

Article 1: This outline is specifically formulated to improve normal education throughout Jiangsu Province.

Article 2: Based on the current establishment of provincial normal schools, the province is tentatively divided into six normal school districts, as follows: The first district, with Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Normal School as the central district, includes the eleven counties of Zhenjiang, Danyang, Jiangning, Jiangpu, Jurong, Liuhe, Gaochun, Lishui, Yangzhou, Jiangdu, and Yizheng. The second district, with Provincial Wuxi Normal School as the central district, includes the ten counties of Wuxi, Wujin, Yixing, Liyang, Jiangyin, Jingjiang, Jintan, Wuxian, Wujiang, and Changshu. The third district, with Jiangsu Provincial Taicang Normal School as the central district, includes the twelve counties of Taicang, Kunshan, Jiading, Shanghai, Songjiang, Nanhui, Qingpu, Fengxian, Jinshan, Chuansha, Baoshan, and Chongming. The fourth district, with Jiangsu Provincial Huaiyin Normal School as the central district, includes the nine counties of Huaiyin, Huaian, Siyang, Lianshui, Shuyang, Suqian, Gaoyou, Baoying, and Funing. The fifth district, with Jiangsu Provincial Donghai Normal School as the central district, includes the ten counties of Donghai, Tongshan, Fengxian, Pei County, Xiao County, Dangshan County, Pi County, Sui County, Ninghai, Guanyun, and Ganyu. The sixth district, with Jiangsu Provincial Rugao Normal School as the central district, includes the nine counties of Rugao, Nantong, Taixing, Dongtai, Taixinghua, Yancheng, Haimen, and Qidong.

Article 3: The provincial normal schools and rural normal schools within each normal school district shall be jointly responsible for improving local education in their respective districts, with the provincial normal schools taking the lead.

Article 4: Local early childhood education and women's education improvement matters within each normal school district shall be temporarily handled by the Suzhou and Xuzhou Women's Normal Schools, respectively. The methods for this shall be agreed upon by the two schools and submitted for approval.

Article 5: Each normal school district shall immediately organize a District Normal Education Improvement Research Association, jointly composed of the provincial normal school, other normal schools within the district, affiliated elementary schools, experimental elementary schools, and county education bureaus. The organizational charter shall be drafted by the provincial normal school in each district, convening a meeting of all schools and bureaus within the district mentioned above, and submitted to the Education Department for approval and record.

Article 6: The tasks of the Normal Education Improvement Research Association in each district are as follows: 1. Investigate and compile statistics on the supply and demand of normal school students. 2. Study matters related to the training of normal school students. 3. Study matters related to normal school equipment, teaching, and enrollment methods. 4. Examine the service performance of normal school graduates and provide guidance and encouragement for their continued studies. 5. Study matters related to normal school student visits and internships. 6. Study matters related to the connection between normal schools and local education. 7. Other matters related to the improvement of normal education.

Article 7: Each normal school district shall establish two or three local education supervisors, depending on the size of the district and the number of schools. Their duties shall be defined separately.

Article 8: Complete the teacher supply and demand survey statistics for each normal school district within a specified time limit, as a standard for establishing, adding, or reducing schools and grades in the province's normal education for the next year. The methods are as follows: A. The Normal Education Improvement Research Association in each district shall formulate a survey form and submit it to the Department for review and approval, ordering the county education bureaus to conduct a thorough and responsible investigation according to the form, completing it within the time limit. B. If any county education bureau fails to conduct the investigation effectively or fails to submit the report by the deadline after receiving the Department's order, they shall be immediately subject to disciplinary action for negligence. C. Based on the teacher supply and demand statistics obtained from each district, and taking into consideration the specific local education conditions of each district, compile a design plan for the province's normal education schools and grades.

Article 9: Establish rural normal schools in phases to seek the balanced development of rural education.

Article 10: Strictly define the admission and service restrictions for normal school students, listed separately as follows: 1. Regarding admission: A. Those with poor character who have been dismissed from other schools shall not be admitted. B. Those who are not dedicated, lack proper demeanor, have unclear speech, or are unable to be simple and hardworking shall not be admitted. C. Those who are physically weak or have hidden illnesses shall not be admitted, even if their test scores are excellent. D. Married male and female students shall not be admitted. They shall not marry after enrollment until graduation. If they marry midway, they shall be ordered to withdraw from school, and the school shall recover tuition, board, and lodging fees from their parents and guarantors. 2. Regarding service: A. The restrictions on service shall be handled in accordance with the recently formulated Regulations on Service for Normal School Graduates by the Education Department. B. Matters concerning service allocation shall be handled by the county education bureaus in consultation with the Normal Education Improvement Research Association in each district.

Reorganized Donghua Football Club 87

Formulating an Outline for Improvement Plan

Hiring Li Silian as Instructor

Chen Jinjiang and Qiu Junong as Directors

Friendly Match with British Army Scheduled for Tomorrow

丨Mr. Sheng Pingchen Actively Striving for Improvement丨

Recently, the news of the reorganization of the Donghua Football Club has been widely spread. People who are enthusiastic about it are scrambling to inquire about the exact situation of the reorganization and the plans for the future. Various newspapers have published reports. The following is a detailed record of the Donghua reorganization process and plans:

The motive for organizing Donghua was entirely due to Mr. Sheng Pingchen's feeling that after the dispersal of the Yuehua team, there was a lack of a strong football team in Shanghai to show the strength of the Chinese. With the support of people from all walks of life and the consent of former Yuehua team members Zhou Xianyan, Chen Yu, and Li Qing, the team was painstakingly organized. Since its establishment, although it has only been a year, it has been able to occupy a considerable position in the Shanghai football scene and has been praised by people from all walks of life. Unfortunately, the January 28th Incident suddenly occurred, and all industries in Shanghai were affected, and football matches were invisibly suspended. Since then, the football atmosphere in Shanghai has become so cold that no one has consulted about it. The work of the Donghua Football Club has also become silent. Due to the war, some team members traveled to Southeast Asia, some retired to their hometowns, and some joined other summer football clubs for entertainment. Mr. Sheng temporarily shelved the matter due to the lack of direction. Now, as the various industries are recovering after the war, people from all walks of life have also been aroused by the enthusiasm of the summer football matches and have awakened and recalled the old events of Donghua. They inevitably speculate due to their enthusiastic hope, resulting in many misunderstandings. However, Mr. Sheng is making every effort to plan a good direction for the Donghua club affairs, so as to thoroughly reform it. Mr. Sheng, since the initial organization of Donghua, has painstakingly managed it, and at the same time felt various inconveniences. Therefore, with the consent of Mr. Zhou Xianyan, (this matter was around mid-July this year), he convened a meeting of Donghua football team members to discuss and strive for a reform plan. The team members then decided to elect Mr. Chen Jinjiang and Mr. Qiu Junong as directors to draft a thorough reform plan. In order to avoid being unable to do so, Mr. Sheng, Mr. Qiu, and Mr. Chen discussed and widely sought out numerous enthusiastic giants and people from all walks of life to jointly discuss and study the fundamental plan to consolidate the foundation. In addition to Mr. Sheng continuing to maintain the status quo, another large-scale outline and plan will be formulated, and in the future, it will be developed step by step according to the outline. It is heard that the outline will be drafted and announced soon, hoping that the society will criticize and support it. It is also heard that the club has now hired Mr. Li Silian as a football instructor. It is heard that Mr. Li has drafted concrete training methods, and the team members' skills will be further improved in the future. It is learned that in order to practice, the team has specially invited the Shanghai-based British Army football team to play a friendly match at the China Baseball Field tomorrow (Tuesday) afternoon. It is expected that the Shanghai football fans who have been separated from Donghua for a long time will once again flock to Rue Pere Robert, vying to see the skills of the Donghua athletes after the reorganization as soon as possible. The side of the China Baseball Field will also restore the enthusiastic scene of the past.

All-American Tennis Tournament Still Belongs to Vines 89

Straight Sets: Cochet Completely Convinced

True Skill, Worthy of the King of Kings

New York, Forest Hills, 10th: Vines, the All-American and Wimbledon champion, proved today that he is indeed one level higher than Cochet. In today's singles championship final of the All-American Tennis Tournament, Vines defeated Cochet in straight sets to retain the championship.

Three Consecutive 6-4 Scores: Vines' performance was wonderful, full of confidence and determination, to defeat his strong opponent. The first set was 6-4, the second set was also 6-4, and the third set was still 6-4.

Cochet's Second Failure: This is Cochet's second failure to Vines. The first time was the Davis Cup final between France and the United States, where Vines won in five sets, with scores of 4-6, 0-6, 7-5, 8-6, and 6-2.

Allison Continues Play and is Eliminated: Allison and Cochet's replay continued this morning after each winning two sets yesterday and the game was unfinished due to darkness. As a result, Cochet won the deciding fifth set 7-5 with a score of three to two and gained the right to play in the final. The five set scores were 1-6, 12-10, 6-4, 3-6, 7-5.

Aftermath of the Davis Cup: Cochet has not been to the United States for four years. This time he crossed the Atlantic to compete with Vines. Who is higher and who is lower? The French said that the failure in the Davis Cup at that time was different, because France had already won the United States three to one and retained the silver cup. The gain or loss of the fifth group was no longer important. Therefore, not many people attached importance to Vines' victory at that time. Now that the true skill has been seen, there is nothing to argue about.

The Truth About the Davis Cup Dispute: Moreover, at that time, the Davis Cup final between France and the United States increased the frustration and resentment of the American team due to Vines' victory over Cochet. On the first day of the final, the United States lost both singles matches. On the second day, they recovered one point in doubles. Therefore, if they could win both singles matches on the third day, they would win back the silver cup. In the last two singles matches, Barrocutra first played against Allison. In the first and second sets, Allison won with scores of 6-1 and 6-3 respectively. However, Barrocutra won the third and fourth sets with scores of 6-4 and 6-2, tying the score at two to two. In the deciding fifth set, Allison was ahead with a score of 5-4. In the tenth game, Allison won another point and was about to win the game. When Barrocutra served, 12,000 people in the audience were worried for Barrocutra. The first ball touched the net. The second ball would determine Barrocutra's fate. According to Allison's observation from the moment the racket was raised, the ball was a few inches outside the serving boundary line, and he thought he had won and went straight to shake hands with Barrocutra. However, looking back, the linesman did not call the ball "out," and the referee followed suit. Allison was stunned at this time, full of resentment. The joy turned to hatred, and the audience was in an uproar. Allison was so angry that he could not control the ball and ended up failing with a score of 7-5. The American team's glimmer of hope for the Davis Cup was ruined by this linesman. Isn't that tragic? Whether France or the United States will win this year's Davis Cup is still an unresolved issue in the public opinion.

Commercial News

Finance 90

Last Week's Gold Market Initially Fell, then Rose

Over the past week, the gold market experienced slight fluctuations and a state of confusion, which was ultimately difficult to suppress. Although there were no excessively large waves, the price fluctuated by six or seven taels daily. Within the industry, bullish and bearish trends diverged. Initially, due to the recovery of overseas silver markets and frequent increases in exchange rates, the price broke through the 700-tael mark, opening at 698.8 taels. Subsequently, due to the loosening of local bills of exchange, a low price of 693.2 taels was suddenly seen on Tuesday, marking four consecutive days of decline. Afterwards, advances and retreats were sudden, hovering around 700 taels. Furthermore, although the silver market continued to rise, Shanghai bills of exchange tended to move in the opposite direction due to settlement requirements. Gradually, the gold price shifted from weak to strong, and the rising trend became more intense. The silver market began to shrink, and the Central Bank vigorously absorbed spot goods, resulting in fewer reserves in the market. Gold delivery chips became increasingly scarce, and the market price soared sharply. On Friday, the momentum was unparalleled, breaking through the 710-tael mark and reaching 717.8 taels. However, due to conflicting foreign news on that day, there were fluctuations. Afterwards, it seemed to reverse and decline slightly, resulting in 712.6 taels. Overall, compared to the previous week, it continued to rise by 11.4 taels, with a total difference of 24.6 taels between the highest and lowest points of the week. The opening and closing prices differed by a rise of 13.8 taels. The bond market environment can be said to have been without any changes. Spot Yarn Consumption Became Even Quieter

At the beginning of last week, the situation for cotton yarn was extremely weak. Scattered short sellers, due to sluggish real demand, dumped their holdings in unison. However, the long position of Rongxing remained steadfast, and the two sides, long and short, held their ground strongly. Unexpectedly, the US cotton government's estimate, released on September 8, showed a slight increase in production, and the market plummeted. The local people were greatly shocked, and the long sellers were disappointed. The market dropped by 3 taels. However, the long position of Yongan Kang not only did not sell but instead bought in and increased its position. Scattered households mostly tended to sell short, resulting in an increasing number of open account transactions. Currently, the inventory of various factories is still low. Strong Downtrend Observed in Cotton Futures Last Week 94

US Cotton Production Quantity Increased

In the past week, the cotton market experienced a very large decline. Because of the booming output of Ningbo Jinyi Yaohua cotton, there was deep concern about low prices in the future market, so large-scale hedging sales were carried out on the exchange. On Monday, more than 40,000 dan were sold, and the market fell by more than one tael. The firm upward momentum in Shanghai was broken. Before long, because the trend of US cotton was still good and Japanese merchants had news of purchasing Chinese cotton for export, the spot cotton situation in the market was unusually brisk, and market prices recovered slightly. However, a certain manufacturer sold off whenever prices rose. It was found that the amount sold was as large as 160,000 dan, and it was finally suppressed. However, Yongan Factory absorbed it on dips, about 60,000-70,000 dan. In terms of the general trend of the cotton market, the price of Chinese cotton is relatively cheap, so there is occasional news of foreign merchants bundling and exporting it. According to a portion of the purchased futures quantity, the amount is considerable. Currently, because this year's harvest is still good in all directions, and new cotton is being listed vigorously, sellers are taking the opportunity to suppress prices. If the US cotton 8-fen mark can stand firm and the gold price is around 700 taels, the future of Chinese cotton still has good prospects. Unexpectedly, the US government's second estimate, released on August 8, showed that the production quantity not only did not decrease, but also increased slightly, resulting in New York cotton prices plummeting by more than one cent. The stable situation of cotton futures was also completely broken. It was difficult for scattered longs to support the market, and the market fell like a runaway horse down a steep slope, falling a thousand feet straight down, with a drop of more than one tael in one session. But the buyers remained unmoved. It was found that the total transaction volume of cotton futures for the week was 69,700 dan, and the price of each month fell by 1.89 qian compared to the previous week. The sales of spot cotton in the market were relatively lively. Compared to the previous week, US cotton fell by 80 pounds. Grain 97

Pujiang Rice Market Downturn Stabilized

Yesterday, the rice market in South Shanghai was overcast and rainy in the morning. The supply from various guilds was not abundant. Due to the Mid-Autumn Festival approaching and the relationship between accounts and silver, people were calm and transactions were sluggish. Ordinary goods felt more sluggish. New and aged ocean-produced top-quality goods were scarce, and the market felt tight.

Yesterday, the rice market in Xinzha was not active. Although there were many people near the market in the morning, the shops had a calm attitude, and the market situation was difficult to grasp. Changxi North Japonica and early and late rice were lower than the previous day, in fact due to the abundant bottom reserves, and people were bearish. New Japonica and new ocean-produced top-quality goods did not sell well, and transactions by customer guilds were sluggish, making it difficult for the overall market to improve.

Silk and Tea 98

Silk Market Resumed Changes Last Week

New York and Lyon Had Ample Silk Stocks, Factory Purchases Relaxed

Japanese Silk Price Suppression and Dumping Caused Sharp Falls in Silk Prices Again

Over the past week, the overseas raw silk market has resumed drastic changes. European and American silk weavers, in view of the low quality of Japanese silk and the gradual rise in prices, and that Japanese silk cannot be used to weave silk alone, coupled with poor global silk production, have all started to abandon purchasing Japanese silk and instead purchase Chinese silk. The Shanghai silk market has improved daily. However, Japanese silk merchants are keen to compete, and have actively transported large quantities of Japanese silk to European and American markets, so that the stocks of raw silk in New York and Lyon and other ports have suddenly become abundant, and factory purchases have relaxed. Japanese silk merchants then resumed the old trick of suppressing prices and dumping silk in the middle of last week. The price of Japanese silk fell by 170-180 yen, which severely affected Chinese silk, and the price also fell sharply, with a drop of 12 cents per pound. Shanghai silk sales suddenly became quiet and tired on the weekend, and European and American banks were all watching. In the middle of last week, a total of more than 300 packages of spot and futures silk were traded, and more than 200 packages were exported.
