Special Security Precautions in the Chinese Area Yesterday 100

Public Security Bureau Strictly Guarding Against Communists

According to the National Society, the Municipal Public Security Bureau received a tip-off yesterday morning that the Communist Party held a meeting of representatives from various districts and departments of the Communist Party in the rooftop garden of the Sincere Company a few days ago. It was decided that representatives from each district would be responsible for separately notifying workers in various factories in the Shanghai West and East areas to unanimously assist unemployed workers throughout Shanghai. On the afternoons of the 7th, 9th and 10th, the Communist Party's false Central Committee convened a secret meeting in Shanghai of all executive committee members and executive committee representatives from various districts and departments in Jiangsu Province to promote communism, distribute reactionary leaflets, and carry out riots. Because the authorities in both the Chinese and French concessions had received reports in advance and ordered strict precautions, the meeting did not take place. Later, it was changed to 6 pm yesterday (the 11th) for a secret meeting in the Rue Mazellan area of the French Concession to convene a meeting, organize a parade and demonstration, and launch a riot, taking the opportunity to gather in the Tangjiawan area of the Chinese area and distribute leaflets on Zhonghua Road and Minguo Road, etc. After receiving the report, the bureau notified the Police Department of the French Municipal Council, closed the iron gates at Tangjiawan, Nanyang Bridge, and other intersections between the Chinese and French concessions, and ordered the police chiefs of various districts to order special precautions. The entire inspectors of the Supervision Department and the entire detectives of the Detective Team were ordered to go to various intersections to be on alert (implementing inspections in case of suspicious persons). There were also police patrols and vehicle patrols to take separate routes to prevent and curb chaos.

Solicitation targets: (A) Freelance professional groups, (B) Various legal entities, (C) Various trade associations, (D) Commercial associations of various roads, joint associations of citizens in various districts, (E) Various hometown associations, (F) Various national goods groups, (G) Various factories, (H) Various companies and shops. 3. New member fee standards: (A) Group members: 10 to 100 yuan per year; (B) Shop and factory members: 10 to 50 yuan per year. 4. Divisions: (A) Honorary Captain, (B) Honorary Staff Officer, (C) Commander-in-Chief, (D) Deputy Commander-in-Chief, (E) Chief of Staff, (F) Deputy Chief of Staff, (G) Names of various divisions (to be held by all temporary executive and supervisory committee members). 5. Organizations, shops, factories, or individuals who join the association through solicitation shall fill out an application form. The application form must be signed and stamped by the applicant and the introducer. 6. The application forms issued by each division must be stamped with the division's seal for identification. 7. When collecting application forms, each division shall immediately collect membership fees from the applicant, along with the application form, and submit them to the association's accounting department to obtain a receipt for the membership fee, which will be forwarded to the applicant. 8. The association will issue membership certificates to organizations, shops, and factories that join the association. Individual members will be issued badges by the association. Both will be processed after the formal general membership meeting is held. 9. This plan will be implemented from the date of its approval by the association's joint executive and supervisory committee meeting.

Pudong Native Place Association Requests the Restoration of the Gaoqiao Municipal Office 108

The Pudong Native Place Association received a letter from members Ma Baosen and others regarding the abolition of the Gaoqiao Municipal Office, requesting that it be forwarded to the government for restoration. The standing committee members of the association submitted a document to the municipal government, stating: "Submitting a report on the local panic caused by the abolition of the Gaoqiao Municipal Committee Office, requesting a review and approval for restoration." According to a letter from members Ma Baosen, Shen Zhen, Xie Bingchong, Zhou Ruiting, Li Chengfu, Yin Shijie, and Huang Shixi, Zhong Renjie, a member of the Gaoqiao Municipal Committee, suddenly resigned, and the Municipal Committee Office was immediately abolished. It is deeply feared that the autonomous administration will suddenly change to the old rules. Speculating on the future, we are extremely frightened. We implore you to submit a petition on our behalf and reinstate the office to assist the government and maintain the local area. Gaoqiao District used to belong to Baoshan and is located in the northern part of Pudong, bordering the sea to the east, the Wusong River to the west, and controlling the mouth of the Yangtze River to the north, facing Wusong. Its location is important. I have long heard that your government is strongly planning to develop Gaoqiao, because although Gaoqiao is located in Pudong, transportation is convenient, and the influence of foreign merchants is sometimes infringed upon. Therefore, if we do not plan for the development of municipal administration, it is fine. If we plan for the development of municipal administration, we should start with this district. In the past, when preparing for autonomy, Gaoqiao was designated as a district, and it was naturally considered necessary in fact. Now that Committee Member Zhong Renjie and Yang Hongjun of the Fahua District, which is connected to the concession, have resigned one after another, and the respective offices of the Municipal Committee Members have been abolished at the same time, the Committee Members Zhong and others may have resigned because of the difficulty of handling affairs and yielded to the virtuous. Your government should choose people for the area. It seems that it is impossible to give up eating for fear of choking. It is understood that Shanghai City was originally composed of nineteen cities and villages, and later divided into forty autonomous regions. The reason why the municipal committees are not set up in the South Shanghai and Zhabei areas is that there are relevant bureaus nearby. Secondly, the municipal committee in Yinxiang Township was abolished in the eighteenth year because it was designated as the city center. Now, Gaoqiao is far away from Yinxiang and north of Luhang and Gaohang in Pudong. Setting up a municipal committee to establish the pioneer of local autonomy will make a model district for our Shanghai City. This is what our association has been looking forward to day and night. If it is abolished one day, all municipal affairs will be taken over by the relevant bureaus. So that the local people must go to various bureaus for extremely trivial matters, dividing the whole into parts, which is extremely inconvenient. However, the Gaoqiao Fahua districts each abolished their offices at the time of the committee members' resignation. Outsiders will not misunderstand that the survival of the municipal office follows the advance and retreat of the individual committee members, or is it a punishment for the committee member's poor handling of affairs, and the office is abolished to satisfy the desire for quick results? The members of the association are difficult to remain silent on the sections of the letter from Ma Baosen and others. Now, only for the sake of Gaoqiao District, for the sake of municipal administration, this Gaoqiao District is far outside of Luhang and Gaohang. In other words, it can be said that it is a relatively remote place. Before there were municipal committee offices in various districts of the city, it seemed that it was not possible to make an exception to abolish them first. Please review and approve and quickly submit it to the municipal conference for reconsideration and restore the Gaoqiao Municipal Committee Office as soon as possible. As for the selection of committee members, whether to retain Zhong Renjie or to select and appoint from local people, it is up to you to decide. We dare not participate in the last discussion. We respectfully submit this report, hoping that you will review it. Sincerely submitted to Wu, the Mayor of Shanghai, by Du Yong, Mu Ouchu, Huang Renzhi, Shen Menglian, and Lü Yuequan, the standing directors of the Pudong Native Place Association.

Recent Freight Situation After the Implementation of Responsible Transportation 113

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, since the first day of this month, the Jinpu Railway and the Huning and Ningbo-Shanghai Railways have stipulated that responsible transportation will be implemented on a trial basis at eight stations, including Shanghai North Station, Maigen Road, Coal Port, Nanjing, Shanghai South Station, Rihui Port, and Hangzhou Zhaokou. As of yesterday, responsible transportation was implemented uniformly at all stations on the two railways. The degree of reduction in freight volume in the first ten days has attracted considerable attention. Yesterday, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency specially investigated the actual quantities in the transportation industry. The number of train tons shipped from Maigen Road Station in October is compared with the freight situation in the ten days before the implementation of responsible transportation as follows: In the first ten days of September, a total of 78 cars of goods were shipped out, totaling 2,358 tons, of which 16 cars (393 tons) were for Nanjing Station (responsible transportation), including 13 cars of sugar (311 tons), 1 car of paper (21 tons), 1 car of matches (21 tons), and 1 car of iron (40 tons). In the last ten days of August (before the implementation of responsible transportation), a total of 115 cars of goods were shipped out, totaling 3,255 tons, of which 41 cars (1,133 tons) were for Nanjing Station. By comparison, the total freight volume decreased by 28 percent, while the freight volume under responsible transportation decreased by 65 percent. It can be seen that the freight situation is slack after responsible transportation.

The Suffering of the Grain, Bean, and Rice Industries Under Responsible Transportation 114

Reply to the Ministry of Railways

The Shanghai Grain, Oilseed Cake Industry and the Bean and Rice Industry Associations submitted a reply to the Ministry of Railways yesterday, stating: "The railway's change to responsible transportation has both increased freight rates and complicated procedures. From the standpoint of merchants, our association has listed seven points of more obvious disadvantages in the general rules and sent a letter to the Ministry of Railways requesting detailed instructions and disclosing these opinions in the newspapers. Subsequently, the Ministry of Railways provided explanations, and the party committees of the two railways went to great lengths to correct them. After careful analysis, there are still some things that cannot be said. The Ministry of Railways explained, 'The ministry's resolute reforms are actually to relieve the suffering of merchants and the people.' The party committees of the two railways corrected, 'Implementing responsible transportation is precisely to facilitate the public.' The words are not unpleasant, and the intentions are not bad. However, to seek the actual implementation of responsible transportation, freight rates are increased by 10 percent, and special priority and highest priority categories are set up, with freight rates increased by 30 to 60 percent. Can the suffering of merchants and the people be relieved by this? Moreover, in the past, when goods arrived at the station, there was still a six-day storage period. Storage rent was charged only after the deadline. Now that transportation is responsible, the general rules stipulate that goods must be picked up within six office hours. The restrictions are so tight that merchants will not be able to pick up their goods on time and will often be charged the so-called storage fees and late fees. The collection is planned and certain to be obtained. Moreover, the reporting procedures are cumbersome and complicated. Is it possible to facilitate the transportation of the public in this way? Regarding the pick-up of goods, the Ministry of Railways also believes that goods arriving at the station at night are not calculated according to working hours. Because the twelve hours from 6:00 PM to 6:00 AM the next morning are not working hours, the twelve-hour limit for unloading is actually equal to eighteen hours. The party committees of the two railways said that the railway bureau has now been changed to 24 hours. Tasting the two statements, the intentions are the same. Since the railway bureau considers the time from 6:00 PM to 6:00 AM to be non-working hours, it should be known that our merchants are also resting during these twelve hours and cannot only do the work of unloading. Therefore, what the Ministry of Railways calls equal to eighteen hours and what the party committees of the two railways call having been changed to 24 hours are still equal to six office hours after restoration. The reason for deliberately making this statement is probably to cover people's eyes and ears. Furthermore, the Ministry of Railways said that the layers of exploitation suffered by passengers and merchants under non-responsible transportation are definitely not limited to this 10 percent. The actual expenditure of freight is 40 to 100 percent or more. The party committee said that merchants actually feel the pain of expensive freight due to the handling of the previous transportation business by intermediaries, but they did not mention it. Is this statement true? Those who handle transportation can seek clarification of the facts. However, according to the experience of our association members, apart from the Jinpu Railway, the number of forwarding companies established for the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways is large, and the competition among the members is extremely fierce. The handling fees charged are extremely low. It has never been heard that it is as expensive as 40 to 100 percent or more. If the handling fees for past freight transportation really had layers of exploitation of 40 to 100 percent, then the merchants would surely applaud and rush to comply with the railway's 10 percent increase in freight rates. Why would they bother with words and rise up in opposition? It should be known that in recent times, disasters have occurred frequently, and disturbances have been frequent. Industry and commerce have declined, and this has reached its extreme. This phenomenon has long been seen in the Ministry of Railways' insight. It has taken advantage of its disadvantages to increase its burden and make the merchants sick again. It is appropriate that merchants have no choice but to abandon railway transportation and turn to water transportation. It is the railway that forces it to do so. How can merchants like to do this? Recently, in February, more than one million bags of wheat, grain, and beans were shipped to Shanghai. According to the association's investigation, the goods were completely shipped by ship. The trend of goods transportation had gradually turned to water transportation before the railway increased fees. Then, how will the impact of increasing fees by 10 percent be like? There is no need to ask the elders. Thinking that this will be used to develop the entire national railway business can only be regarded as an ideal. Applying it to reality, I am afraid it will be counterproductive. To sum up, 1. Increasing freight rates not only runs counter to the purpose of relieving the suffering of merchants, but also affects the cost of goods, hinders the progress of foreign trade, merchants change to water transport, and car transport is robbed. According to the highest principle of developing industry and increasing the railway business, it is obviously inconsistent. It should be requested to cancel the order to increase freight rates by 10 percent. 2. Since the name of responsible transportation is responsible transportation, then all procedures such as car dispatching, car delays, and custody are the responsibility of the railway. Why should they be listed as miscellaneous fees, causing the end of car staff making things difficult and demanding and covering the suspicion of layers of exploitation? Should be asked to consider removing them. 3. The purpose of priority and highest priority is to cleverly obtain superior freight rates. The result will inevitably lead to the stagnation of ordinary freight and force it to compete for priority. Therefore, the so-called car dispatching, detention, and change fees are collected. This kind of chain reaction plan is really the source of greed. It should be requested to cancel it. 4. Before the responsible transportation, the storage period after the goods arrived at the station was six days. After the implementation of responsible transportation, it was stipulated that the goods must be picked up within six office hours. In fact, merchants cannot handle it at all, and the treatment is also very unfair. It should be requested to restore the old example.

Recommendations from the Wenzhou-Chu Salt Affairs Improvement Association to Rectify the Ou Salt Sheds 117

The Wenzhou-Chu Salt Affairs Improvement Association of this city recently telegraphed the Transportation Office, advocating for the reorganization of the Ou sheds. The original text is as follows: "We have recently received a letter from our members Chen Shu and others, stating that the corruption in Wenzhou-Chu salt affairs is the worst in Zhejiang Province. The root cause lies in the malpractices of salt merchants over the past four years. Officials and merchants collude, leading to skyrocketing salt prices, causing immense distress to the people, who have nowhere to turn for redress. Fortunately, the contracting system has been abolished, and freedom has been granted. All the residual evils left over from the contracting period should be thoroughly eradicated. Upon investigation, various salt farms in Wenzhou, such as North Salt Shuangsui and Ledong Lexi of Changlin Farm, had salt sheds established before the contracting system. The factory brokerage, commission, and spring labor costs collected by each shed were submitted to the office by the farm bureau for approval and collection, consistently without any changes. Since the implementation of the contracting system in Wenzhou-Chu, although the old salt sheds nominally continued to operate, they were, in reality, controlled by the contractors everywhere, leading to the closure of sheds run by honest and weak individuals, while cunning individuals colluded with the contractors. As a result, the contractors converted the old sheds into public offices, bribed the authorities to collect salt, increased factory brokerage commissions, and arbitrarily imposed various fees such as canopy charges. Depressing purchase prices and selling at inflated prices has become a common practice among the factories, and North Salt factories even engage in selling at reduced prices. All these malpractices originated from the contracting system, and a thorough investigation would immediately reveal the truth. Recently, with the abolition of the contracting system, the salt collection offices established by the contractors have been submitting applications to change their names to salt factories, while maintaining the same old practices. This indicates that although the contractors are gone, their residual evils remain. We are specially writing to this association, requesting that you forward this to the department for review, bestow upon us the favor of reorganization, and strictly enforce prohibitions." The association convened a meeting on the solar day of this month to discuss the matter. Everyone agreed that the points raised by member Chen were indeed factual and urgently needed reform. Consequently, the following resolution was adopted and submitted to your esteemed office: "That all factory owners and brokers in Wenzhou, and all fees, be uniformly changed back to the rules that were in place before the implementation of the contracting system. Those that were already established in the past should be thoroughly reorganized, and those that are now requesting to change should be strictly prohibited. As for the various fees arbitrarily collected by Wang merchants, please follow the Ministry's telegram and implement prohibition rules to handle them separately. The bad habit of government offices in our country is often to shelve orders from superiors as the only way to solve difficult problems. Over time, various parties have treated it as the only way to handle major cases, delaying progress and turning them into pending cases, leading to the failure of laws and regulations and the unbridled behavior of evildoers. Now, fortunately, the Minister has the determination to reorganize salt affairs, and you, sir, have expressed the intention to thoroughly remove accumulated malpractices. Swift and decisive action is in your hands. Correcting past mistakes and anticipating expectations are within reach. We believe that a wise man like you will thoroughly investigate and implement laws and regulations, eliminate abuses, and promote benefits, to satisfy the longings of the people of both Wenzhou and Chu. (Below omitted.)"

East Asia Jute Bag Factory Workers Are Organizing a Union 120

Opposing Capitalist Oppression

A Notice Urges Workers to Unite

The East Asia Jute Bag Factory on Robison Road in West Shanghai is a Japanese-owned enterprise, divided into more than ten departments, including hemp beating, fine yarn, and bobbins. It employs approximately 1,200 male and female Chinese workers. After the outbreak of the Shanghai War, it suspended operations for more than two months and resumed work on April 20th. The union has leased space at 26 Huaxing Lane, Robison Road, to begin registration and has issued a notice to workers stating:

Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau's Relief Plan for Unemployed Workers 121

Original Text of the Second Outline: Welfare for Workers

The issue of unemployed workers in this city has long been a concern for all sectors of society. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has drafted a draft relief plan for unemployed workers, which has been reviewed by the bureau's third consultation meeting and then submitted for further review to ensure prudence. It is understood that the plan is very detailed and divided into four main outlines. The second outline is excerpted below:

The Unemployment Problem: The unemployment problem has become the most serious and intractable social problem in the world today. According to the latest statistics from the International Labour Office, in April of this year, the number of unemployed workers in the United Kingdom was 2,204,740; in Germany, 6,034,100; in France, 347,446; in Italy, 1,053,016; in Japan, 485,290; and in the United States, the number of unemployed union members alone reached 184,000. Due to China's industrial backwardness and the collapse of the rural economy, the number of unemployed and jobless people cannot be estimated. Even in this city, there are no accurate statistics to rely on. According to the results of the bureau's trial unemployment statistics in 1929, the number of unemployed union members in the city accounted for 6.45% of the total number of members. In recent years, industry has become increasingly depressed, and it has been affected by the January 28th Shanghai Incident. The labor unrest is more serious than it was when the National Revolutionary Army arrived in Shanghai in 1927. The unemployment problem is a comprehensive economic problem that cannot be solved locally. From a proactive perspective, developing the national industry is a more thorough solution. However, the development of a country's industry must have sufficient conditions and cannot be achieved overnight. The central government has long formulated meticulous industrial and commercial plans for our country. Since this draft focuses on providing relief to unemployed workers in this city, it should take into account the unemployment situation of workers in this city and, within the scope of the bureau's authority, select those measures that can be implemented effectively within a reasonable period and to a reasonable extent.

Relief Outline: Specific plans are proposed, divided into the main points of eliminating labor-capital disputes, organizing welfare projects for workers, promoting the rural economy, and developing industries. Passive measures to treat the symptoms and proactive construction plans are listed together. Those matters that involve national affairs, such as tariffs, immigration, and reclamation, will be suggested to the National Government at any time and will not be listed separately. However, for the implementation of the plan to provide relief to unemployed workers, both financial and human resources are indispensable. When this draft was first drafted, there were no corresponding regulations for the supply of financial and human resources, so the scope of relief, although determined, lists the main points of relief and the outlines of the measures. For matters that are within the responsibilities of the responsible departments, such as the elimination of labor unrest, the guidance of labor union facilities and the labor movement, the inspection of factories, the establishment of workers' savings associations, labor schools, clubs, and consumer cooperatives in various factories, and the improvement of agricultural affairs, the encouragement of side businesses, the promotion of domestic goods, the guidance of commodity sales, and the implementation of scientific management, the responsibility lies with labor and capital, while the bureau takes a supporting and supervisory position. It is not difficult to order the responsible departments to implement them effectively in order. Those that require additional special funds to be raised will be determined by the director based on their importance and urgency, and implemented in order. Below is the original text of the second outline for organizing welfare projects for workers.

Welfare Projects for Workers: Organizing welfare projects for workers, such as employment agencies, small-scale craft lending offices, workers' savings associations, and raising unemployment relief funds, are all relief measures after unemployment. The purpose of the other projects is to improve workers' knowledge and skills, improve workers' living conditions, and thus coordinate labor and capital, develop industry, and prevent unemployment. The following welfare projects for workers, from the first to the ninth, are the first step of work, are important, and have the possibility of being organized, and should be organized immediately. Items ten through twenty-one are the second step of work and should be organized when sufficient funds are raised or when there is a sufficient opportunity.

Preliminary Work: (A) First Step of Work (To be Organized Immediately) (1) Organize an Unemployment Research Committee to study unemployment and explore relief measures and implementation. (2) Organize a Municipal Employment Agency. (Explanation) The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has now promulgated temporary measures for employment agencies, and this city should comply with them to fulfill its responsibility to adjust the supply and demand of labor. (Measures) Draft the articles of association for the Municipal Employment Agency of this city in accordance with the temporary measures for employment agencies promulgated by the Ministry, and prepare a budget and submit it to the Municipal Government for approval. (3) Organize a Small-Scale Craft Lending Office (Explanation) If workers in bamboo ware, rattan ware, and other crafts can be loaned funds to purchase materials when they are unemployed, they can make them themselves. Not only will their skills not be wasted, but they can also earn a living from it. (Measures) Draft the articles of association for the Small-Scale Craft Lending Office, prepare a budget, and submit it to the Municipal Government for approval. Start with a trial in one area, and expand it after it is successful. (4) Supervise factories to establish workers' savings associations. (Explanation) The central government has now promulgated temporary measures for workers' savings, and this city should comply with them and supervise factories to establish workers' savings associations to handle workers' savings matters. This project is run by the factories themselves, and the bureau fulfills its supervisory duty. (Measures) Draft the temporary measures for workers' savings and the detailed rules for implementation in this city, and supervise factories to establish workers' savings associations. (5) Supervise factories to establish labor schools or labor classes. (Explanation) Labor education is divided into three types: literacy training, civic training, and vocational training, to increase workers' knowledge and skills and improve their work efficiency. The two departments of industrial and educational education have jointly formulated an outline of implementation measures for labor education, stipulating that factories, companies, shops, etc., should establish labor schools or labor classes. This project can be jointly handled with the Education Bureau. (Measures) Draft the outline of implementation measures for labor education with the Education Bureau and the detailed rules for implementation in this city, and supervise factories, etc., to establish labor schools or labor classes. (6) Supervise factories to establish staff clubs. (Explanation) The purpose of clubs is to promote noble entertainment and improve the lives of staff and workers. Too few factories have staff clubs, so they should be supervised to establish them universally in accordance with the general outline of the industrial and commercial staff club plan promulgated by the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce. (Measures) Draft the detailed rules for the implementation of the general outline of the industrial and commercial staff club plan in this city, and supervise factories to establish staff clubs. (7) Supervise labor unions to establish consumer cooperatives. (Explanation) The organization of consumer cooperatives is based on the spirit of equality and mutual assistance, pooling funds, and supplying the necessities of life in the most economical way in order to improve living conditions. Labor unions or factories should establish or assist in establishing them in accordance with the law. (Measures) The temporary general rules for consumer cooperatives in this city have already been promulgated, and labor unions should now be supervised to establish consumer cooperatives. (8) Supervise factories to organize other welfare projects for workers. (Explanation) For example, factories that employ female workers should set up childcare facilities, and those that usually employ more than 300 workers should set up medical rooms, etc. (Measures) Send personnel to investigate the situation in various factories and supervise or persuade them to organize within a possible scope. (9) Investigate the welfare projects for workers that have already been organized in this city. (Explanation) How many welfare projects for workers have been organized by labor unions, factories, or public offices in this city, and what is their content? It is not yet known in detail and should be investigated first before supervision and guidance can be carried out. (Measures) Send personnel to investigate and supervise the registration.

Second Step of Work: (B) Second Step of Work (To be Organized When the Opportunity Arises) (10) Raise funds to build labor housing (for families). (11) Raise funds to build labor dormitories (for singles). (12) Raise funds to build labor canteens. (13) Raise funds to build municipal labor clubs. (From items 10 to 13, these are welfare projects organized by the government for workers in small workshops and occupational workers, such as construction workers, dock workers, and rickshaw pullers.) (14) Raise funds to build labor childcare facilities. (15) Raise funds to build labor kindergartens. (16) Raise funds to build labor schools. (From items 14 to 16, these are welfare projects to reduce the burden on workers and educate labor children.) (17) Raise funds to build a labor insurance company. (18) Prepare to add labor hospitals. (19) Raise funds to build labor cemeteries. (20) Raise unemployment relief funds. (21) Organize other welfare projects for workers.

Wen Hongen Dispatches Personnel to Inspect Various District Offices 122

Wen Hongen, the newly appointed director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, has been reviewing all case files submitted by various sections, departments, and teams since taking office a few days ago and has completed the sequential deployment. He has not yet had time to deal with the personnel rosters, uniforms, and military equipment of the various district offices under his jurisdiction. Therefore, Wen ordered Chief Inspector Gong Xicheng yesterday to dispatch personnel to inspect them. Strictly Prohibit Military Personnel from Riding Trains Without Tickets 123

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have previously been ordered by the Ministry of Railways to open and consult the Ministry of Military Administration to instruct their subordinate troops to strictly prohibit and ban military personnel from riding trains without tickets. However, recently, military personnel have frequently been riding trains without tickets at various stations on the two railways and forcibly occupying first and second-class seats. When the military police accompanying the train reasoned with them, disputes often arose. Therefore, the Ministry specially consulted the Ministry of Military Administration to issue another order strictly prohibiting this. If military personnel need to travel by train on official business, they must be issued a Class A military travel permit by the Ministry and present it to the station to exchange for a ticket before they can board the train. In the future, if military personnel attempt to board the train without a ticket, the military police accompanying the train should detain them and hand them over to the responsible officer for severe punishment.

Measures for Punishing Loafers at Docks 124

At the wharves in this city, there are often unemployed vagrants who disturb travelers. The Public Security, Public Utilities, and Social Affairs Bureaus specially consulted on four measures for punishment the other day, as follows: 1. Loafers arrested by the wharf management of the Public Utilities Bureau in South Shanghai will be the responsibility of the Public Security Bureau to escort to the vagrant work-study center for accommodation. 2. The expenses for the aforementioned loafers' food and clothing at the center will be the responsibility of the Public Utilities Bureau to raise. 3. The procedures for detaining and sending wharf loafers will be determined separately by the Public Security and Public Utilities Bureaus. 4. The vagrant work-study center should quickly find ways to expand its buildings and increase the number of people it can accommodate.

Impersonating the Public Works Department Inspector and Committing Fraud 125

Lei Wenkui Previously Committed Crimes in the Chinese Area

Xie Wanfang, a Chinese detective of the Yulin Road police station, previously apprehended three individuals: Ye Fangyan from Hangzhou, Cheng Fengxiang from Tongzhou, and Li Changyou from Ningbo. They were impersonating inspectors from the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, extorting money from Liu Jinyou and others at 233 Taopeng Road by claiming that the construction of wooden sheds on the rooftop and other violations were not allowed. They were handed over to the First Special District Court, where they confessed that their leader was Lei Wenkui from Nanxiang. As a result, they were sentenced to imprisonment. Recently, Detective Xie, who handled the case, learned that the criminal Lei was hiding at No. 5 Huasheng Road in the French Concession. He and a Western detective, along with French Concession police officers, secretly went there at 1:15 PM, arrested Lei, and three accomplices, Wan Aru and Dong Bin from Ningbo. They seized one pistol, one hundred bullets, several badges, and a box of cards. A pair of handcuffs were found near Dong. Lei and Wan claimed that the pistol was bought from Wang Fuxiang, a native of Jiangbei, who lived at 999 Donghan Bili Road in the Public Concession. The detectives then arrested Wang and brought him back to the police station for detention. The next morning, they were escorted to the Fourth Criminal Court of the Special Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, recounted the previous events, stating that Lei's card was printed with "Lei Wenbiao." He claimed that Lei had previously committed similar fraud cases in the Chinese area and had been punished, so he changed the "biao" character. The gun, bullets, and other evidence were presented for inspection. Lei Wenkui had committed numerous fraud cases in Nanshi, and the Municipal Public Security Bureau should transfer him. He claimed he had not committed any crimes in the Concession. When questioned, Lei Wenkui confessed that he had known Ye Fangyan for many years and had committed crimes with Ye and others in Nanshi. He was arrested and sentenced. He was released from prison on March 11th of this year and, unable to find a livelihood, planned to commit similar illegal acts, impersonating inspectors from the Public Security Bureau. That is why he had the badges and cards. He had now obtained a position as an inspector in the Fisheries Administration Bureau and needed a pistol for self-defense on the ship in the Huangpu River, so he asked Wang Aru to buy one from Wang Fuxiang. Wan was a friend of Ye Fangyan and stayed with him. Wan Aru confessed that Lei asked him to buy the pistol for protection while working on the ship, which was true. Wang Fuxiang confessed that Wan Aru came to him, showed Lei's card, and he bought the pistol from a man named Meng. Dong Bin also confessed that he was an inspector on the Fisheries Administration Bureau's ship and that the handcuffs were for arresting pirates. His other statements were evasive. Judge Lin reviewed the confessions and ordered all defendants to be detained and remanded for further investigation at a later date.

Manchurian Railway Business

Since the September 18th Incident last year, the Japanese have progressed from economic and cultural aggression to acts of occupation. However, the pioneers of this process are still economic and cultural activities, and the company responsible for them is the South Manchuria Railway Company (Mantetsu). We all know that the Japanese have established four main organs in the three northeastern provinces: the Kwantung Army Headquarters, which manages military affairs; the Kwantung Government-General, which manages civil administration; the Consulate, which manages foreign affairs; and Mantetsu, which manages economic and cultural enterprises. Before the September 18th Incident, the mask had not yet been fully removed, so the military, civil, and diplomatic aspects of the four organs still maintained a pretense of cordiality. Only Mantetsu, using commercial operations as a shield, openly proceeded, infiltrating all subsidiary enterprises outside the railway. Many Chinese people were shocked but perhaps unable to fully understand. Time has passed, and it has been a year since the incident. Looking back at the pain of lost territory and the suffering of displacement, we must study it even more carefully. Here, we selectively describe the Manchurian Railway's business to inform the Chinese people of what to be wary of.

The emergence of the Manchurian Railway's business originated from Japan's acquisition of the South Manchuria Railway rights. The Japanese obtained it after the Russo-Japanese War, succeeding the South Manchuria section of the Chinese Eastern Railway, and also made agreements regarding the Andong-Fengtian Railway and the connecting of Jilin-Changchun Railway with Korea, and the construction of a branch line in Yingkou.

Originally, although the Japanese had set foot in South Manchuria and Andong, there were corresponding time limits. When Yuan Shikai declared himself emperor, he proposed the Twenty-One Demands, changing the South Manchuria and Andong Railways to ninety-nine years, and proposing to revise the Jilin-Heilongjiang agreement. Although the Twenty-One Demands were not recognized by us, the urgency of Japan's intentions is evident. Furthermore, in 1913, there was a proposal to build five railways using Japanese loans: the Sipingjie-Taonan Railway (220 miles), the Kaiyuan-Hailong Railway (123 miles), the Taonan branch of the Changchun line of Jilin-Changchun Railway (180 miles), the Jilin-Hailong Railway (112 miles). Although the Chang-Tao and Ji-Hai Railways could borrow foreign funds, they first had to obtain Japan's consent, revealing their intention to annex.

The establishment of the Manchurian Railway led to the creation of the South Manchuria Railway Company. Since the South Manchuria Railway Company was the source of economic and cultural strategies, it devoted itself to managing the South Manchuria Railway, gradually extending to other related railways in the Northeast provinces and other subsidiary enterprises. Since this article focuses specifically on the Manchurian Railway, we will leave aside Japan's overall plan for all railways in Manchuria and Mongolia and focus on those related to the Manchurian Railway. In fact, all of Japan's overall plans that have been realized can be said to be related to the Manchurian Railway.

In addition to those related to Japan, other railways in the Northeast provinces include the Shenyang-Haikou Railway (state-owned), the Jilin-Hailong Railway (officially and privately operated), the Harbin-Hailun Railway (officially and privately operated), the Qiqihar-Kesha Railway (officially and privately operated), the Hulin-Gangkao Railway (privately operated), the Kaiyuan-Fengcheng Railway (privately operated), the Qiqihar-Angxi Railway (officially and privately operated), the Datong-Tongliao Railway (branch of the Beining Railway), the Jinzhou-Chaoyang Railway (branch of the Beining Railway), the Xinmin-Shenyang section of the Beining Railway (state-owned), the Chinese Eastern Railway (Sino-Russian joint venture), the Muling Railway (Sino-Russian joint venture), and the Beining Railway (British loan). Among these, 24.2% were self-operated, 37% were related to British and Russian interests, and 38.7% were related to Japan. Even the South Manchuria Railway alone far surpasses other railways. The South Manchuria Railway transported 15.96 million tons of goods last year, while all the others combined transported only 18 million tons, accounting for 89%. In addition, the South Manchuria Railway transported 10.576 million passengers, while the other ten railways combined transported only 16.276 million passengers, with a slightly smaller difference, accounting for 65%. If we add other railways related to Japan, the strength of its influence would be immeasurable. The South Manchuria Railway Company was founded in 1906, established by the Japanese after obtaining the right to inherit the Changchun-Dalian section of the Chinese Eastern Railway. According to the original agreement, the Chinese Eastern Railway was based on the loan agreement of the 26th year of the Guangxu reign, with the railway being managed by Daosheng. Therefore, the contract included 5 million taels of silver in capital from the Chinese government. After eighty years, all assets would be returned to China without compensation, and China could redeem them with investment after sixteen years. In fact, it was merely a commercial agreement for a railway loan, but the Japanese obtained it and aggressively expanded their ambitions, actively proceeding. Our government also failed to consider sovereignty and impose restrictions, allowing it to grow out of control and become the vanguard of aggression. The capital of the Manchurian Railway was 200 million Japanese yen, with the Japanese government using railway and mining assets as half of the capital, and the remaining half being raised as commercial shares in Japan. It was moved from Tokyo to Dalian and began operations on April 1, 1907. Twelve years later, the share capital was expanded to 440 million yen, with government and commercial shares each accounting for half, each with 4.4 million shares. It operated the 437.5-mile Dalian-Changchun section, the 31.6-mile branch line from Zhoushuizi to Lushun, the 3.6-mile branch line from Dafangshen to Liushutun, the 13.4-mile branch line from Dashiqiao to Yingkou, the 9.7-mile branch line from Yantai to Yantai Mine, the 3.8-mile Fushun line, and the 170.9-mile Andong line, totaling 670.5 miles. Its strategic location and connections allowed it to control the transportation of Manchuria and Mongolia.

Outside the South Manchuria Railway, the Sipingjie-Taonan Railway branch line reached Tongliao, totaling 264.8 miles. The Manchurian Railway invested 32 million yuan, and the Zhengjin Bank invested 5 million yuan. It was difficult for it to become China's state-owned railway, and due to the loan relationship, everything was almost controlled by the Japanese. The three departments of general affairs, engineering, and transportation were also headed by Japanese directors, and the vehicles used were mostly leased from the South Manchuria Railway, demonstrating the Manchurian Railway's influence.

The Taonan-Angxi Railway was 224.0 miles long. Because of its important location in northern Manchuria, the Japanese intentionally planned to seize it. This railway was nominally contracted by the East Asia Company, a Sino-Japanese joint venture, but the capital actually came from the Manchurian Railway's advance payment, totaling 18 million Japanese yen. The contract stipulated that the loan should be repaid upon completion. If it was not repaid within six months, it would be converted into a loan. Later, we were unable to repay the loan, so it was converted into a loan agreement, and the Manchurian Railway appointed four directors.

The Jilin-Changchun Railway was 127 miles long. In the 33rd year of the Guangxu reign, a loan agreement was negotiated, allowing the Japanese to invest half of the capital. The Manchurian Railway managed it during the 30-year loan period. Thus, the railway rights fell into Japanese hands. It was nominally state-owned, but in reality, it was all controlled by the Manchurian Railway. The administrative organization even included a so-called Manchurian Railway representative, who operated alongside the director. In addition, the three departments of transportation, engineering, and accounting were all headed by Japanese personnel.

The Jilin-Dunhua Railway, which extended 365 Chinese miles further east, would reach Huning in Korea and eventually Qingjin Port. Therefore, it could also be considered a section of the Jilin-Korea Railway. The construction contract was also contracted by the Manchurian Railway in 1925 for 24 million Japanese yen. The Jilin-Korea Railway was most closely related to Northeast defense and was strongly opposed by the people. However, once it reached Dunhua, it could easily connect to Huning, and there was also the Tianbao Mountain-Tumen River Railway, which connected to the Korean Huning Railway at Sanfeng across the river. The Tianbao Mountain-Tumen River Railway was managed by another company with a capital of 4 million Japanese yen, half from the Jilin provincial government and half from the Oriental Colonization Company, but the actual power was again in the hands of the Japanese.

The Wengcheng Railway was one of the light railways in the three northeastern provinces, 124,000 meters long, with a capital of 570,000. The Manchurian Railway held 70% of the shares, and the Benxi Lake Coal Mine held 30%, which was also within the sphere of influence of the Manchurian Railway. In addition, the Jinfu Railway, within the Japanese leased territory of the Jinzhou Peninsula, was 102 kilometers long, practically a Japanese railway.

The South Manchuria Railway's business, in addition to railways, encompassed everything in detail. In the economic sphere, it included locomotive factories, ships, harbors, marine products, mining, iron smelting, postal services, and telecommunications. In culture, it had primary, secondary, specialized schools, and libraries. Furthermore, there were central research institutes, geological survey institutes, scientific research institutes, agricultural experiment stations, veterinary research institutes, and the Manchu-Mongolian Resources Museum. Its various investments had reached over 67.175 million yuan the previous year. Among minerals, the Fushun Coal Mine was the largest, with reserves of 1 billion tons, producing 17,000 tons of coal per day, with an investment of 130 million Japanese yen. The mining area was one li long and four li wide. The Yantai Kuanchengzi Coal Mine was also directly managed by the Manchurian Railway, and there were also indirect investments. Its iron manufacturing was the Anshan Ironworks, located at Anshan Station, with three British-German-style iron-smelting furnaces, producing 1,200 tons per day. It also had ore-dressing and iron-burning equipment, generating 26,000 kilowatts of electricity. In addition, it was equipped with affiliated sulfuric acid-ammonia plants, coal tar distillation plants, wood alcohol plants, naphthalene plants, sulfuric acid plants, and brick factories. Japan was short of steel, so the Manchurian Railway spared no effort in managing it, using it as an external treasury.

The harbor and maritime department spent 69 million Japanese yen annually, and the shipping assets spent 4 million Japanese yen annually, mainly for managing and developing Dalian Bay. It built a 4,100-meter breakwater that could accommodate 30 large ships of 230,000 tons, making it the best harbor in East Asia. In addition, the ports of Gan Jingzi, Lushun, and Yingkou were also managed by the Manchurian Railway due to their geographical advantages. However, in terms of shipping, it was transferred to the Dalian Steamship Company after 1922. The factories directly managed by the Manchurian Railway were roughly as described above, including machinery, power generation, oil refining, gunpowder, gas, and raw material manufacturing such as sulfuric acid. It had almost everything, and its indirect investments in Japanese factories in the Northeast provinces were too numerous to mention. Roughly speaking, it was involved in glass, wool weaving, sugar making, medicine, lumbering, steamships, engineering, insurance, trust companies, and exchanges, but it is impossible to list them all in detail.

In terms of cultural enterprises, the Manchurian Railway ran a medical university, various Manchurian education specialized schools, South Manchurian Institute of Technology, various middle schools, various girls' high schools, various vocational schools, various supplementary schools, kindergartens, libraries in Dalian and Fengtian, and other libraries and kindergartens, totaling more than 50. There were 398 primary schools, 86 middle schools, and 5 specialized schools or higher, and its research and propaganda publications numbered nearly ten thousand.

Local facilities were also under the concession rights of the Manchurian Railway. The management of city streets in Dalian, roads, bridges, embankments, parks, markets, slaughterhouses, hospitals, sanatoriums, firefighting, sheep breeding, chicken farming, milk, etc., were all managed by it. The maintenance costs came from the people's city taxes, supplemented by the Manchurian Railway. The affiliated lands of South Manchuria and Andong were also purchased by it, and even local administrative power was under its management. In essence, the Manchurian Railway area was not just a railway company but a local authority. The Japanese economic base in the Northeast provinces was clear.

Appeal of Russian Beggar's Death Case Scheduled for Hearing 128

The case of Russian beggar Georgi Ladi Kiv, who died in the Second Special District Court detention center in the French Concession on June 19th of this year, was initiated by the police department based on a report from the deceased's brother, Simon Graiteki, who claimed that his brother was beaten to death by the detention center staff. Two Nephews Accuse Uncle of Embezzling Funds 129

Amounting to No Less Than Hundreds of Thousands of Dollars

Xu Yuchen, a shareholder of Hengtong Qianzhuang on Beijing Road, is the second son of Xu Yongyi, a palace guard who was one of the three gentlemen executed by order of Empress Dowager Cixi during the Boxer Rebellion. Xu had three sons: the eldest, Shiming; the second, Shizhong (i.e., Yuchen); and the youngest, Shiheng. After the palace guard was martyred, his wife, Madam Cha, led the family south and resided in Shanghai. In 1905, Xu Yongfu, the brother of the palace guard, divided his brother's estate into four portions. The sons of the eldest son, Shiming, Wenrong, and the sons of the youngest son, Shiheng, Wenxin, each received one portion. Yuchen also received one portion, and the remaining portion was set aside as public property, to be managed by Yuchen since Shiming and Shiheng were deceased, and Wenrong and Wenxin were still young. This has been the case for 28 years. The annual income from pawnshops and land rentals in their hometown of Haiyan and Shanghai is considerable. Madam Cha also used public funds for social expenses. After Madam Cha's death in 1923, the annual expenses decreased. Since Yuchen has been managing the funds and has not provided an accounting, Wenrong and Wenxin have no knowledge of the amount of accumulated public funds. They have repeatedly requested that their uncle provide an accounting, but Yuchen, claiming his seniority, refuses to let his nephews inquire. Now that Wenrong and others have grown up and established the Tiancheng Yarn Company on Avenue Edward VII, they are deeply dissatisfied with their uncle's embezzlement of public property. In the summer, they hired lawyer Ersen to file a petition with the First Special District Court, requesting the preservation of evidence and ordering Xu Yuchen to submit all income and expenditure records from 1923 to 1931 for review. Although the court ruled that he should provide the accounting, Yuchen consistently refused, leading the two nephews to formally sue him. Judge Yang Peng concluded the trial, recognizing the plaintiffs' request as legitimate and ruling that the defendant should submit all accounting records and immediately declare provisional execution. The defendant initially ignored the ruling, then filed an appeal. Finally, as the court's execution became increasingly urgent and police officers were repeatedly dispatched to Hengtong Qianzhuang and his residence at 14 Singapore Road to arrest him, he was able to temporarily stall, but it was difficult to delay indefinitely. At the end of last month, after having an accountant review the accounting books, he complied with the ruling and submitted them, while also withdrawing the appeal. Wenrong and others then began auditing the accounts, and the results revealed numerous acts of embezzlement, estimated to be no less than hundreds of thousands of dollars. To maintain the common interest, they again hired lawyer Ersen to file a criminal private prosecution with the First Special District Court, requesting that the defendant Xu Yuchen be arrested and tried in accordance with Article 356 of the Criminal Law. The court has already approved the issuance of a summons for the defendant and has scheduled a hearing within days. It is reported that Xu Yuchen is over sixty years old and has been suffering from old age and illness. Upon receiving the court summons, he immediately entrusted lawyers Yang Linzhi, Ye Shaowu, and Zhang Jiahui to appear in court to defend him.

County Government Advises Merchants Not to Use "Flying Flowers" 130

The Shanghai County Government recently received a report from the County Farmers' Education Hall, stating that the local cloth of Pudong has always been famous, but in recent years, merchants have been adulterating it with "flying flowers," causing the cloth to be loose and fragile and easily damaged. If this continues, no one will buy it. Therefore, they requested a public announcement prohibiting the use of "flying flowers." The County Government considered that "flying flowers" had not been determined to be contraband and was therefore not in a position to prohibit it. Yesterday, it instructed the various Public Security Bureaus to advise merchants not to use "flying flowers" any further to maintain the reputation of local cloth.

Request for a Dance Denied, Dancer's Face Punched 131

Tang Aifei Accuses Xue Juexian et al. of Assaulting and Humiliating Her in Public

Cantonese opera star Xue Juexian, accompanied by friends Feng Ruiting and others, went to the Xinxin Ballroom on Guizhou Road at 8:15 PM on September 3rd (Saturday) to dance. Xue suddenly had a conflict with dancer Tang Aifei at the ballroom. Feng immediately reached out and punched Tang in the left cheek, injuring her left eye. Tang then hired lawyer Qian Ying to file a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the First Special Court, accusing Xue and Feng of assault. The indictment stated that the plaintiff had been practicing dancing since childhood and had been working as a dancer at the Xinxin Ballroom for years. On the evening of September 3rd, the first and second defendants entered the ballroom to dance. It was early autumn, and there were many guests. At 8:15 PM, as the music began, the first defendant approached the plaintiff and asked her to dance, but she politely declined because she had a prior engagement with another guest. Unexpectedly, a moment later, the first defendant asked a waiter to summon the plaintiff to his table. As soon as she stood there, the second defendant stood up and said, "You have made my friend lose face. Today, my friend has ordered me to hit you." As he spoke, he punched the plaintiff's left eye, causing injury, swelling, and bruising. Witnesses on the scene included the plaintiff's sister, Tang Hongfei (also a dancer at the Xinxin Ballroom), and others. Although the plaintiff's profession is humble, her words and actions have always been extremely cautious. The first defendant, because the plaintiff refused to dance with him, harbored resentment and instigated the second defendant to assault and humiliate her in public, violating Article 293 and Article 324 of the Criminal Law. They should be severely punished, and all rights to file an ancillary civil lawsuit are reserved. Furthermore, the defendants are all residing in temporary lodgings (Room 69, Xinxin Hotel) and have no fixed address, so there is a risk of flight. In accordance with Articles 41 and 42 of the Criminal Procedure Law, they should be arrested as soon as possible. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui of the Fifth Criminal Court of the Special Court issued a summons, but the defendants did not appear. Xue Juexian hired lawyer Wu Chengyu to defend him, stating that Xue had gone to Hangzhou on business on the 8th and could not attend court. He also stated that Xue and others no longer resided at the Xinxin Hotel. Xue now lived at 92 Anle Lane, Jing'an Temple Road, and Feng lived at 13 Hongfu Lane, North Henan Road. Future summons should be sent directly to their residences, and they would be able to attend court. The court then questioned Tang Aifei, who stated that she was 18 years old, from Guangdong, and a dancer at the Xinxin Ballroom. She briefly described what happened. Then, her sister, Tang Hongfei, and an English sailor, Sidaigu, who was present at the time, testified about Feng Ruiting's assault and humiliation of Tang Aifei. Since the defendants did not appear, Judge Liu ordered the case to be postponed for a week and the defendants to be summoned to court for further questioning.

August Work of the Public Works Department Legal Department 133

Number of Cases: The acting director of the Public Works Department Legal Department reported in August that the number of cases prosecuted this month in the Shanghai First Special District Court and the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court totaled 9,832. Among these, 6,973 were minor cases where the bail was confiscated due to non-appearance in court. There were 70 private prosecution cases, of which 41 were withdrawn due to insufficient evidence. A total of 2,818 criminal cases, both major and minor, were concluded. 2,651 individuals were sentenced, 167 acquitted, and 56 cases received suspended sentences.

Appeals: The Public Works Department filed 5 appeals in August. 65 appeals were concluded, including 5 to the Supreme Court, 47 to the High Court, and 13 to the local appeals court. 48 private appeals were concluded this month, including 2 declared not guilty, 35 appeals rejected, 1 appeal withdrawn, 3 cases remanded for retrial, and sentences reduced in 7.

Transfer Cases: This month, local authorities outside the boundary requested the transfer of 11 cases involving 13 defendants. 12 of them have been transferred due to established preliminary evidence. The remaining one was released due to lack of evidence. Three prisoners held since July were transferred this month to the requesting agency. In addition, there were two prisoners each from June and July, awaiting the requesting agency to provide supplementary evidence.

Tax Cases: Sixteen stamp tax cases occurred this month, two of which were withdrawn. The remaining were fined ranging from ten to one hundred and twenty yuan. The special patrol team continued to perform its duties in cigarette tax cases. This month, eight search warrants were requested, three searches yielded no results, six summonses were requested, eight cases were prosecuted, six people were sentenced, and two were remanded.

Unresolved Cases: At the end of August, there were 55 new cases pending in the High Court branch and the Special District Court. There were also pending appeals: 60 in the Supreme Court, 68 in the High Court, and 10 in the local appeals court, totaling 193 unresolved cases. In addition, there were 11 cases with defendants in custody.

Other Matters: In August, the police station executed 8,519 criminal summons, and judicial police executed 361. Civil summons totaled 9,407. Additionally, 946 prisoners were released under the amnesty.

Bomb Explodes, Two Apprentices Seriously Injured 141

At No. 45 Coal Cinder Road, Zhabei, a copper and ironware workshop specializes in manufacturing steel beds and selling them to various steel bed stores. There are many apprentices in the workshop. At 4:35 PM yesterday, the apprentices were picking up iron pieces in the scrap iron pile usually collected at the back door when they suddenly found a bomb. The apprentices, not knowing what it was, vigorously hammered it with iron hammers. With a loud bang, the bomb exploded, injuring two apprentices. One, aged fifteen, had both fingers blown off. The other, aged sixteen, had his right hand blown off and immediately fell to the ground, unconscious. The craftsmen in the workshop heard the sound and came out to see what had happened. They immediately hired a car to take the two apprentices to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. Director Zhang diagnosed them separately. One apprentice was permanently disabled, and the other only had his fingers blown off. He was bandaged with medicine and both were hospitalized for treatment. The police in charge of the district also sent officers to inspect the back door of the workshop and questioned the owner of the workshop in detail about the cause of the accident for verification and handling.

Sayings of the Ninety-Three-Year-Old Ma Xiangbo 161

A Speech Prepared for Receiving the League of Nations Investigation Team 162

— Recorded by Jing.

When the League of Nations investigation team first arrived in Shanghai, General Zhu Ziqiao originally prepared to entertain them and invited Old Man Xiang to participate. Old Man Xiang instructed them to prepare a speech and asked Mr. Hu Gangfu to announce it on his behalf at the time. Later, the proposal to entertain them was cancelled, so the prepared words remained until today. Here is a summary.

"The League of Nations investigation team has consistently upheld justice and has not been deceived by Japan's false propaganda. Therefore, we Chinese people's representatives are very willing to sincerely express our long-standing spirit of loving peace, and declare our future attitude of actively defending ourselves and resisting to the end.

China has always loved peace since ancient times. We not only hope to live in peace, but also are always prepared to die in peace. If you have ever browsed Chinese history books, you must know the custom of living cemeteries in the Six Dynasties. Many literati and scholars sang about this graveyard prepared in life. They even lived in that living cemetery, thinking it was open-minded, and calling themselves understanders. This custom is an ironclad proof that Chinese people still seek peace in death, let alone those who are still alive who would not seek peace? This view is indeed the common psychology of the Chinese people and their inherited spirit of peace. Since you have come to China for justice, please investigate the relics of the Shanghai-Songhu war! You must know that what was destroyed were Chinese shops, what was trampled on were Chinese farmlands, and more importantly, countless innocent Chinese old, young, women, and children were brutally killed by the Japanese formal army! Did you see this phenomenon when you passed through Japan? I will propose to preserve the destroyed battle traces in Zhabei and never rebuild them, as a memorial area, so that alliances for world peace, such as the League of Nations disarmament, can learn from it!

Thank you for your efforts for justice! We Chinese people will never beg you to take sides! I have already sacrificed for peace, and will seek guarantees for peace, and be loyal to peace and defend myself to the end!"

Wives of Fishermen 163

— Zhou Wu-ai

| Qingdao Returnee's Talk |

Verdant foliage forms a canopy, allowing fishermen from their floating boats to catch sight of the renewed joy after a long absence. A carpet of lush green, occasionally interspersed with a few wildflowers, covers the golden sands of the beach where seagulls circle and fly. From the boats, houses are not visible, only these layers of color. As the setting sun casts its glow, one might see the red light of the evening glow reflected from the mountaintops, bathing the scene above, as children frolic on the shore. This is Qingshan: a small village of two to three hundred households, nestled between the sea and the mountains. It is inhabited by wives left behind by their husbands' fishing lives, leading solitary existences, along with a small number of men engaged in trade and the elderly, infirm, and young. In Qingshan, there is no intellectual progress, nor is there reverence for ritual and propriety. All they possess is need. Driven by need, they work and live the same lives day after day.

However, sometimes needs are not fully met, leaving them unfulfilled. The husbands have gone to catch fish, in large or small boats, sailing in groups across the sea. They are gone for ten or eight days, even two or three months, leaving the young women behind. Therefore, driven by need, they have created something that other villages dare not do. They welcome and lodge unfamiliar men, if their husbands are not at home.

| Ah, Sister-in-law! Can I have a cup of tea? I'm so tired. A man with surging desires, seeing that there is no picture from a cigarette pack on the door of this house, will know that she is dreaming a lonely dream: he can go and flirt with her, for a price of two or three yuan.

They are very robust, with curvy breasts and hips, despite their bound feet. Although their children all have a father, his lineage is impossible to trace.

Insect Love 165

Bing Ding

| A Model for People |

In the past, people often used mandarin ducks to describe love, but in fact, the most prone to change in love are insects: insects are most able to sing, aren't they singing love songs? Insects are most able to dance, aren't they dancing? Insects are most able to mate, aren't they practicing "living together in love"? Insects are most able to fight, aren't they fighting for females? They even stay together for life in the skeleton of a sponge, never willing to part like swallows, like the "eternal companions in the same cave" produced in the Mediterranean. Where can people match their unchanging changes in love?

Zoologists say: Male insects also have testicles, vas deferens, seminal vesicles, and ejaculatory ducts in their bodies. Females also have ovaries, seminal receptacles, oviducts, mucus glands, and vaginas. The structure is very complete. So we often see flies carrying flies and dragonflies biting dragonflies in summer and autumn: if they did not know how to change love, first, they would not be so intimate; second, as foreigners say: two flies after three months, the offspring multiplied, would not have to circle the earth dozens of times. There is also the love of ants, which is at a certain time: at this time, everyone grows wings and dances in the air, then holds a wedding. At other times, they work peacefully, not like people who want to fall in love at any time.

The beauty of butterflies and ladybugs is a symbol of love. The male and female crickets follow each other, guarding a place, which can be said to be Liang Hong and Meng Guang among insects. Ticks and fleas spend all day talking about love and practicing dancing in bed. Cicadas, katydids, ground crickets, and bell crickets sing love songs day and night, even more enthusiastically than female students singing "Sister, I love you." Only mayflies and silkworms enjoy the least taste of love, and can be said to be the unfortunate ones in the insect world's river of love.

Who Is Qualified to Talk About Saving the Nation 166

— Huang Da-ge

From airplanes flying in the sky to beggars filing lawsuits on the ground, everyone uses "XX to save the nation" as their slogan. To see how earnestly they are saving the nation, I decided to investigate them thoroughly, but I ultimately did not find a single person sincerely saving the nation.

Advising others to save the nation and saving the nation oneself are, of course, the duties of citizens. Why saving the nation requires waiting for others to advise is one question. Forming groups because of saving the nation and each saving their own nation is another question. Where to save the nation and where to start saving is the third question, which is especially important compared to the above.

I have learned about saving the nation's activities in the newspapers; I have also admired the figures saving the nation. The former is to increase titles, and the latter are all consumers of gasoline. How about giving you esteemed and hard-working figures saving the nation the phrase "save the nation with cars"?

Recently, what is presented to us in the newspapers in the same way as the cause of saving the nation: "industrial decline," "national unemployment,"... all rely on your aid. I very much hope that you can spare some of your strength to save the nation to relieve society.

Saving the nation is not just empty talk. Relying on a few car owners to run around will not save what is not saved. If society is not prosperous, individual economies will panic. If people cannot save themselves, how can they save the nation? If the current figures saving the nation do not pay attention to this point, who is qualified to talk about saving the nation?

A Copper Coin 167

— Zong Zhi

| Different Attitudes |

The meaning of a copper coin is different for each class.

A young man of the bourgeoisie accidentally drops a copper coin on the road, and walks past it without paying attention, still talking to his lover.

A company employee drops a copper coin in the crowd, looks back at the ground, and walks on.

A skilled worker drops a copper coin, bends down to pick it up.

A small coolie at the tram station finds a copper coin under the tram, waits for the tram to pass, picks it up and buys a cigarette to eat.

An old woman from the countryside drops a copper coin, squeezes off the tram to pick it up.

A poor peasant woman drops a copper coin, searches through three ridges of fields.

A beggar shouts after people for a long time, calling them "master" and "madam", before finally getting a copper coin.

Silver Threads (11) 168

— Jiang Hongjiao

"Sister-in-law! Open the door quickly! I'm holding two big watermelons, I really can't stand the sun." Someone was calling outside the door.

"Sorry, please wait a moment, I'll come open the door." Yifen Ruo replied from the window upstairs, and hurried downstairs.

In this moment, many thoughts in Commander Yuan's mind, like lightning, like a gust of wind, like summer clouds, arose in countless and very rapid changes. He didn't understand who was upstairs, and who was outside the door. Was Fenruo a widow in name or in fact? He pitied Fenruo, envied Fenruo, and loved Fenruo. He didn't know how to maintain his original central idea, and he didn't know how to deal with the current environment. In a daze, he couldn't help but open the door before Fenruo came downstairs.

"Ah! It's you?" Mr. Wang was so surprised that he dropped the two big watermelons he was holding on the ground, shattering them.

"Who are you?" Commander Yuan was inexplicable, and couldn't find a second sentence other than this question.

Fenruo had already come downstairs. Seeing that all the secrets were completely revealed in front of Mr. Wang, she didn't know what to do, but instead went to pick up the broken watermelons.

"Are you Commander Yuan?" Mr. Wang also calmed down a bit, looking carefully at Commander Yuan from head to toe twice, still not daring to be sure, so he asked again.

"I am Commander Yuan, are you the one selling watermelons?" Commander Yuan also asked.

"Come in quickly and talk!" Fenruo stopped picking up the broken watermelon, and pulled Mr. Wang inside, closing the door.

"Now the scheduled time for the completion ceremony of the monument has passed for an hour: I heard that the county magistrate and the chief of public security just went to the city to welcome the commander, but they came up empty, and they have returned, and are still waiting for the commander to attend the meeting to hold the ceremony." Mr. Wang faithfully reported, and while he spoke, he often scanned back and forth between Commander Yuan and Fenruo with his eyes, like a hunting dog, trying to detect some special meaning.

"Mr. Wang, Commander Yuan is her relative, | saying that she moved her lips upstairs | he came to see her illness by the way, in any case, please don't publicize it, this is my earnest request to you." Fenruo almost tearfully begged Mr. Wang to keep the secret.

"Sister-in-law has instructed, I will definitely do as instructed, and I have also decided: but in any case, Commander Yuan should wait for at most half an hour, and must attend the meeting, because today's ceremony is extremely grand, and there are many guests who want to give speeches, if it is later, the time will be tight.

Supplement to the Shanghai Shenbao

Words

Wearing a Homespun Long Gown 169

— Buddha

Wearing a homespun long gown was originally a common occurrence for us intellectuals. We cannot afford Western woolens and fine silks, and the price is also expensive (although it is slightly cheaper this year), so we have to wear a homespun long gown and sway around. It is not considered a big deal. If a person of the propertied class or someone with a considerable status were asked to wear a homespun gown, they would feel out of place and unable to see friends. In this world that "only values clothing and not people," there is such a situation.

According to a Hong Kong telegram yesterday, Deng Zeru proposed to the Political Committee to prohibit wearing foreign clothes, but it was not passed because it was difficult to implement. However, the provincial government issued an order yesterday that all civil servants must wear homespun long gowns. At a time when the standard of living is increasing day by day and the trend of extravagance and dissoluteness is rampant, promoting thrift and remembering to save the nation is the responsibility that the authorities should have. However, the Political Committee did not pass it because it was difficult to implement, which is puzzling.

All civil servants must eat. Assuming that this order is promulgated and vigorously implemented, there will never be a reason for them to refuse to wear homespun long gowns and voluntarily resign. Where is the difficulty? It is suspicious. The only ones who think it is difficult are the members of the Political Committee, who are mostly people of the propertied class and those with considerable status. If civil servants wear homespun long gowns while they themselves do not wear homespun long gowns, they would feel a little embarrassed. If they also wear homespun long gowns, it would seem to demean their status and would not be enough to show the authority of the committee members. The difficulty is probably here.

In fact, it doesn't matter. Mr. Feng Yuxiang wears old cloth short clothes, which are not as beautiful and elegant as Guangdong cloth long gowns, but he is still welcomed everywhere and is not treated like a poor Mr. Cai Yuanpei just because he wore an old cloth short jacket. It can be seen that a person's status and personality are by no means different because of the beauty or ugliness of their clothes.

On the contrary, if you are a person without personality, even if you wear very elaborate and authentic clothes, others will never recognize you as a person of personality and status, because there is such a misunderstanding of concepts. Therefore, people who live in cities often earn 20 yuan in salary and spend 19.8 yuan on clothes, which is pitiful and ridiculous.

Our country's production is so backward, and the people's ability to live is so weak, but the authorities are still unwilling to promote thrift as an example. What are their intentions? Taking Shanghai as an example, the most beautifully dressed women are prostitutes. I ask, what is the personality and status of prostitutes?
